State Law reference— V.T.C.A., Finance Code ch. 1 et seq.; finances, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 101 et seq.; V.T.C.A., Tax Code ch. 1 et seq. 
 
SUBCHAPTER I. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
Sec. 34.01. - Annual occupation tax. 
There is hereby levied and there shall be collected from every person, firm, association, or corporation pursuing any occupation under the general laws of the state, an annual occupation tax, equal in each instance to one-half of the state occupation tax, which said taxes shall be paid annually in advance except where otherwise provided by the state laws, in which event the same shall be paid as is provided by the state law. 
(Code 1996, § 34.03; Ord. No. 0038, 11-21-1974) 
State Law reference— Authority to levy one-half of state occupation tax, Tex. Const. art. 8, § 1; occupation tax on oil and gas wells, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 191.081 et seq.; municipal governing body may impose and collect occupation taxes, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 302.101; local occupational tax prohibited unless specifically permitted by state law, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 101.008; occupation tax on coin operated machines, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2153.451.  
Sec. 34.02. - Fee schedule for Floresville Event Center. 
The fee schedule for use of the Floresville Event Center shall be as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time. 
(Ord. No. 2014-005, 5-8-2014)  
SUBCHAPTER II. - PROPERTY TAX[9] 

Footnotes: 
--- (9) --- 
State Law reference— Property tax code, V.T.C.A., Tax Code ch. 101 et seq. 
 
Sec. 34.10. - Levy of property tax. 
(a)  There is hereby levied or adopted a tax rate in an amount to be determined from time to time by ordinance of the city council on $100.00 valuation of property, that tax being levied and apportioned to the specific purposes provided by ordinance. 
(b)  The tax assessor-collector is authorized to assess and collect the taxes of the city, employing the most current tax rate. 
(Code 1996, § 34.01; Ord. No. 0038, 11-21-1974; Ord. No. 132, 9-14-1995; Ord. No. 136, 9-12-1996; Ord. No. 153, 9-25-1997; Ord. No. 167, 9-9-1999; Ord. No. 185, 9-13-2001; Ord. No. 198, 9-12-2002; Ord. No. 223, 9-22-2005; Ord. No. 234, 9-28-2006; Ord. No. 264, 9-25-2008) 
Charter reference— Power to tax, § 9.14. 
State Law reference— Levy of taxes, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 102.009.  
Sec. 34.11. - Purpose. 
The tax hereby levied is levied for the purposes stated in such ordinances, and those specified in and authorized by V.T.C.A., Tax Code ch. 302, and none other, to wit; for current expenses, and for the construction or purchase of public buildings, water works, sewers, and other permanent improvements within the limits of the city and the construction and improvement of the roads, bridges and streets of the city within its limits. 
(Code 1996, § 34.02; Ord. No. 0038, 11-21-1974)  
Sec. 34.12. - County appraisal district map. 
(a)  A county appraisal district map which reflects properties for municipal taxation purposes is attached to the ordinance from which this section was derived and kept on file in the office of the city secretary (Exhibit A), and included by reference as if fully set forth. 
(b)  Exhibit A is hereby adopted as the official record of the city limits as of the date that the city adopted its Home Rule Charter, November 10, 2004. 
(c)  Said Exhibit A defines subsequent annexations through the effective date of the ordinance from which this section was derived. 
(Ord. No. 281, 6-30-2011)  
Sec. 34.13. - Homestead exemption. 
(a)  That the city adopts an allowance of a $15,000.00 homestead exemption for city property owners 65 years of age and over, and for those property owners (regard less of age) who qualify for disability benefits under the Federal Old Age, Survivors, and Disability Insurance Program administered by the Social Security Administration. An eligible disabled person who is 65 years of age or over may not receive the homestead exemption for both qualifying as "65 or over" and "disabled," but may choose either. Each person desiring such exemption shall file an application with the county appraisal district, such application being in a form and filed at such time as shall be required by law. 
(b)  The surviving spouse of an individual who qualified for an exemption under this section for the residence homestead of a person 65 or older is entitled to an exemption for the same property in an amount equal to that of the exemption for which the deceased spouse qualified if: 
(1)  The deceased spouse died in a year in which the deceased spouse qualified for the exemption; 
(2)  The surviving spouse was 55 or older when the deceased spouse died; and 
(3)  The property was the residence homestead of the surviving spouse when the deceased spouse died and remains the residence homestead of the surviving spouse. 
(c)  A surviving spouse is not entitled to an additional exemption under this section if the surviving spouse qualifies for an exemption on his own. 
(d)  That the adopted tax exemption shall be effective for the year 2014 tax year and all future tax years, unless and until the tax exemption is either revised or repealed by city council. If revised, pursuant to article VIII, section 1-b(b) of the Texas Constitution and the V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 11.13(d), such allowance for homestead exemption shall be no less than $3,000.00; however, the city may repeal the homestead tax exemption enacted by this section in its entirety. 
(Ord. No. 2013-009, §§ 2, 3, 10-24-2013) 
State Law reference— Residence homestead, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 11.13.  
SUBCHAPTER III. - HISTORIC DISTRICTS[10] 

Footnotes: 
--- (10) --- 
State Law reference— Tax exemption for historic sites, V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 11.24. 
 
Sec. 34.20. - Historical building tax abatement. 
The owner of a historical commercial building located in the historical district (as defined in chapter 154) may apply for a city property tax abatement on repair and/or restoration costs for both the land and structure on the building site. The land and building will have an annual assessed value equal to the assessed value of the tax year immediately before the repairs and/or restoration was completed, for the next five years following completion of work. The tax abatement will begin the first day of the first tax year after verification of the repairs or the remodeling. For purposes of this subchapter, the term "repairs" or "remodeling" means work performed in accordance with building and construction codes of the city and in accordance with the city design review committee. For purposes of this subchapter, the term "historical commercial building" means any building, 50 years old or over, utilized for nonresidential use as provided in chapter 154. 
(Code 1996, § 34.20; Ord. No. 187, 9-27-2001)  
Sec. 34.21. - Eligibility for tax abatement. 
To be eligible for property tax abatement, the property must meet all of the following conditions: 
(1)  The property must be located within the city limits; 
(2)  The property must contain a historical commercial building as defined by this subchapter; and 
(3)  At the time of application for the tax abatement, the exterior and/or the interior must be in need of repairs. The cost of which (as shown on a legitimate contract or bid) exceeds 25 percent of the assessed value of the structure the year the work is to begin. Only that work for which a building permit, plumbing permit, or other project permit used may be counted on determining whether the work exceeds 25 percent of the assessed value. 
(Code 1996, § 34.21; Ord. No. 187, 9-27-2001)  
Sec. 34.22. - Application for tax abatement. 
An application for a tax abatement must be filed with the county appraisal district and the city code compliance officer. Each application must be signed and sworn to by the owner of the property and must include the following information: 
(1)  The legal description of the property; 
(2)  Detailed plans and documents related to the proposed work showing how the repairs are in accordance with building and construction codes and how restoration is in accordance with the criteria set forth by the city design review committee; 
(3)  A statement and documentation of the cost for repairs of the exterior and interior of the building to show that the costs exceed 25 percent of the assessed value of the structure; and 
(4)  A projection of the construction time and completion date of the repairs. 
(Code 1996, § 34.22; Ord. No. 187, 9-27-2001)  
Sec. 34.23. - Qualification for tax abatement. 
(a)  Upon completion of the repairs in accordance with the city design review committee and/or building and construction codes of the city, the owner shall submit to the county tax appraiser and the city code compliance officer a sworn statement certifying that the repairs have been completed. 
(b)  The owner shall obtain a certificate of qualification for a tax abatement from the county tax appraiser committee signed by the code compliance officer. A certificate of qualification shall not be approved until the applicant files a commitment of immediate repay to the city for all tax revenues not paid because of the tax abatement, if the owner is required to repay the taxes under section 34.24. The commitment must be approved as to form by the city attorney and filed in the county deed records. The commitment shall run with the land and bind the owner and his heirs and assigns. Any unpaid repayment required under section 34.24 shall be a lien against the property in accordance with section 34.20. 
(c)  Once the certificate of qualification is approved, the county appraisal district shall appraise the property in accordance with section 34.20. 
(d)  Once the certificate of qualification is approved, the property shall be entitled to a tax abatement as follows: 
(1)  For the first calendar year following the granting of such certificate of qualification, an abatement of 100 percent of the taxes generated by the increase in value of the property attributable to the repairs or remodeling as described above; 
(2)  For the second calendar year following the granting of the certificate of qualification, an amount equal to 80 percent of the taxes generated by the increase in value of the property attributable to the repairs or remodeling as described above; 
(3)  For the third calendar year following the granting of the certificate of qualification, an amount equal to 60 percent of the taxes generated by the increase in value of the property attributable to the repairs or remodeling as described above; 
(4)  For the fourth calendar year following the granting of the certificate of qualification, an amount equal to 40 percent of the taxes generated by the increase in value of the property attributable to the repairs or remodeling as described above; and 
(5)  For the fifth calendar year following the granting of the certificate of qualification, an amount equal to 20 percent of the taxes generated by the increase in value of the property attributable to the repairs or remodeling as described above. 
(Code 1996, § 34.22; Ord. No. 187, 9-27-2001)  
Sec. 34.24. - Destruction or alteration of historic landmark. 
If the design review committee has reason to believe that a historic landmark that has received a tax abatement, as provided for herein, has been totally or partially destroyed by any cause, or altered by the willful act or negligence of the owner or his representatives in violation of the preservation criteria contained in the policies of the design review committee, then the committee shall immediately cause the matter to be scheduled for the earliest possible consideration by the city council. If the council determines that the historic landmark has been totally or partially destroyed by any cause, or altered by the willful act or negligence of the owner or his representatives, the owner shall immediately repay to the city all of the tax revenues that were not paid because of the tax abatement. 
(Code 1996, § 34.24; Ord. No. 187, 9-27-2001)  
SUBCHAPTER IV. - HOTEL OCCUPANCY TAX[11] 

Footnotes: 
--- (11) --- 
State Law reference— Hotel occupancy tax, V.T.C.A., Tax Code ch. 156; municipal hotel occupancy taxes, V.T.C.A., Tax Code ch. 351. 
 
Sec. 34.30. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this subchapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Consideration means the cost of the room, sleeping space, bed or dormitory space or other facilities in such hotel and shall not include the cost of any food served or personal services rendered to the occupant not related to cleaning and readying such rooms or space for occupancy, and shall not include any tax assessed for occupancy thereof by any other governmental agency. 
Hotel means a building in which members of the public obtain sleeping accommodations for consideration. The term "hotel" includes a hotel, motel, tourist home, tourist house, tourist court, lodginghouse, inn, roominghouse, or bed and breakfast. The term "hotel" does not include: 
(1)  A hospital, sanitarium, or nursing home; 
(2)  A dormitory or other housing facility owned or leased and operated by an institution of higher education or a private or independent institution of higher education as those terms are defined by V.T.C.A., Education Code § 61.003, used by the institution for the purpose of providing sleeping accommodations for persons engaged in an educational program or activity at the institution; or 
(3)  An oilfield portable unit, as defined by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 152.001. 
Occupancy means the use or possession or the right to use or possession of any room, space or sleeping facility in a hotel for any purpose. 
Occupant means anyone, who, for a consideration, uses, possesses, or has a right to use or possess any room or rooms, or sleeping space or facility in a hotel under any lease, concession, permit, right of access, license, contract or agreement. 
Permanent resident means any occupant who has or shall have the right to use or possess a room in a hotel for at least 30 consecutive days, so long as there is no interruption of payment for the period. 
Person means any individual, company, corporation or association owning, operating, managing or controlling any hotel. 
Quarterly period means the regular calendar quarters of the year, the first quarter being composed of the months of January, February and March, the second quarter being the months of April, May and June, the third quarter being the months of July, August and September, and the fourth quarter being the months of October, November and December. 
Tax collector means the tax assessor and collector of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 115.01; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997)  
Sec. 34.31. - Levy of tax, rate and exception. 
(a)  There is hereby levied a tax upon the occupant of any room or space furnished by any hotel where such cost of occupancy is at the rate of $2.00 or more per day, such tax to be equal to seven percent of the consideration paid by the occupant. 
(b)  No tax shall be imposed hereunder upon any persons who are permanent residents. 
(c)  Governmental entity exemption. 
(1)  A United States governmental entity described in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(a) is exempt from the payment of tax authorized by this subchapter. 
(2)  A state governmental entity described in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(b) shall pay the tax imposed by this subchapter but is entitled to a refund of the tax paid. 
(3)  A person who is described by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(d) is exempt from the payment of the tax authorized by this subchapter. 
(4)  A person who is described by V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 156.103(c) shall pay the tax imposed by this subchapter but the state governmental entity with whom the person is associated is entitled to a refund of the tax paid. 
(5)  To receive a refund of tax paid under this subchapter, the governmental entity entitled to the refund must file a refund claim on a form provided by the city and containing the information required by the city. The state comptroller by rule shall prescribe the form that must be used and the information that must be provided. 
(6)  A governmental entity may file a refund claim with the city under this subchapter only for each calendar quarter for all reimbursements accrued during that quarter. 
(7)  The right to use or possess a room in a hotel is exempt from taxation under this subchapter if the person required to collect the tax receives, in good faith from a guest, an exemption certificate stating qualification for an exemption provided in this subsection (c). The exemption must be supported by the documentation required under rules adopted by the state comptroller and the city. 
(Code 1996, § 115.02; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997; Ord. No. 156, 3-12-1998)  
Sec. 34.32. - Collection. 
Every person owning, operating, managing or controlling any hotel shall collect the tax imposed in section 34.31 for the city. 
(Code 1996, § 115.03; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997)  
Sec. 34.33. - Reports. 
On or before the last day of the month following each quarterly period, every person required in section 34.32 to collect the tax imposed herein, shall file a report with the tax assessor and collector showing the consideration paid for all room or sleeping space occupancies in the preceding quarter, the amount of the tax collected on such occupancies, and any other information as the tax collector and assessor may reasonably require, which report shall be in writing. Such persons shall pay the tax due on such occupancies at the time of filing of such report. 
(Code 1996, § 115.04; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997)  
Sec. 34.34. - Rules and regulations. 
The tax collector and assessor shall have the power to make such rules and regulations as are necessary to effectively collect the tax levied herein, and shall upon reasonable notice have access to books and records necessary to enable him to determine the correctness of any report filed as required in this chapter and the amount of taxes due under the provisions of this chapter. 
(Code 1996, § 115.05; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997)  
Sec. 34.35. - Use of proceeds. 
(a)  The proceeds of the hotel occupancy tax levied by this subchapter shall be used at the discretion of the city council, but only for those uses authorized under V.T.C.A., Tax Code ch. 351, subch. B (V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.101 et seq.). 
(b)  The funds are to be dispersed at the direction of the city council by the city secretary. 
(Code 1996, § 115.06; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997; Ord. No. 156, 3-12-1998)  
Sec. 34.36. - Penalty. 
If any person required by the provisions of this subchapter to collect the tax imposed herein, or make reports required herein, and pay to the tax assessor and collector the tax imposed herein, shall fail to collect such tax, file such report or pay such tax, or if any such person shall file a false report, or any such person shall violate any of the provisions of this subchapter, such person shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor, and shall pay to the tax assessor and collector the tax due, together with a penalty as provided in V.T.C.A., Tax Code § 351.004. 
(Code 1996, § 115.99; Ord. No. 155, 12-11-1997)  
CHAPTER 35. - PERSONNEL POLICIES 
 
Sec. 35.01. - Participation in Texas Municipal Retirement System. 
(a)  Election to participate in the TMRS. On behalf of the city, the city hereby exercises its option and elects to have the city and all of the employees participate in the Texas Municipal Retirement System (hereafter TMRS) as provided in V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 851 et seq., and all of the benefits and obligations of such system are hereby accepted. 
(b)  Adoption by reference. Ordinances effecting the plan for participation in the TMRS, employee contributions, updated service credits, increases in benefits and retirement annuities and any other applicable legislation of the city and state are adopted by reference into this Code of Ordinances as if fully set forth herein and shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk. 
(Code 1996, § 35.01; Ord. No. 172, 2-10-2000; Ord. No. 200, 9-12-2002; Ord. No. 226, 11-10-2005; Ord. No. 232, 9-14-2006; Ord. No. 241, 3-22-2007; Ord. No. 243, 4-12-2007)  
Sec. 35.02. - Longevity pay program. 
There is hereby established a longevity pay program to be instituted by the city under the following terms and conditions: 
(1)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Employee means every full-time employee of the city other than the city manager. 
Years of service means the number of full years running from employee start date until December 1 of the current calendar year. If an employee leaves city employment and returns at a later date, the years of service shall be calculated as the aggregate amount of time spent as a city employee. 
(2)  Years of service. 
a.  Each employee's years of service shall be calculated annually on December 1; and 
b.  In the subsequent pay period following December 1, each employee shall be entitled to a payment in the sum of $50.00 multiplied by the employee's years of service. 
(3)  Longevity pay. 
a.  Longevity pay as authorized by this chapter is subject to the availability of funds. This chapter shall be reviewed annually during the city's budget process and the amounts contained in subsection (2)b of this section shall be amended or eliminated as necessitated by the city's budget. 
b.  The first calculation of years of service and payments pursuant thereto shall be on December 1, 2016, and continue annually thereafter. 
(Ord. No. 2015-028, 9-22-2015)  
CHAPTER 36. - INFORMATION TECHNOLOGY DEVICE USAGE POLICY  
SUBCHAPTER I. - APPLICATION OF POLICY 
 
Sec. 36.01. - Scope and purpose of policy. 
The policy provided in this chapter provides guidance for the acceptable use of information technology systems including electronic devices, electronic mail, Internet access, and/or software among other city systems. This includes acceptable use of city-owned computers, mobile devices and/or personal devices reimbursed through city stipends. This chapter establishes and identifies responsibility for the acceptable use of technology to help ensure the confidentiality, integrity and availability of city systems. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.01, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.02. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
City-administered information technology systems means any technology or equipment that is used and/or managed by the city even if the city does not own the technology or equipment. City-managed information technology systems include technology or equipment owned by the city, on loan to the city, funded by grants, leased by the city, etc. The term "information technology (IT) systems" includes, but is not limited to, computers, mobile communication devices, telecommunication devices, servers, networks, software, databases and email messages, among other physical and virtual infrastructure. 
Digital signature means an electronic identifier intended by the person using it to have the same force and effect as the use of a manual signature. 
Electronic mail record means an electronic government record sent and received in the form of a message on an electronic mail system of a government, including any attachments, transmitted with the message. 
Electronic record means a record created, generated, sent, communicated, received, or stored by electronic means. 
Electronic signature means an electronic sound, symbol, or process attached to, or logically associated with a record and executed or adopted by a person with the intent to sign the record. 
Incidental use means personal use of technology that does not interfere with the performance of assigned duties, does not have a detrimental effect on city information technology systems, and is not prohibited by this chapter. 
ITSD means the information technology systems department and is the designated individual or department responsible for maintaining the operation and security of the city's technological environment. 
Local government record retention schedules means publications issued by the Texas State Library and Archives Commission under the authority of V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 441, subch. J, which establishes the mandatory minimum retention period for a local government record except and as where superseded by a records retention schedule adopted by the city as authorized by the Texas Government Code. 
Malware means malicious software designed to impact the confidentiality, integrity and/or availability of an information technology system. Malware can include viruses, worms, Trojan horses, or adware among other malicious programs. 
Network means a group of two or more computers linked together to facilitate communication, data sharing and processing among other computer activities. 
Policy means the technological device usage policy as set forth in this chapter. 
Records management officer means the person who administers the records management program established in each local government under V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 203.026. 
Retention period means the minimum time that must pass after the creation, recording or receipt of a record or the fulfillment of certain actions associated with a record before it is eligible for destruction. 
Sponsor means the departmental representative responsible for authorizing non-employee access to city assets and/or systems. 
User means any employee or non-employee who uses city-administered information assets and/or systems, exclusive of the city's web and/or social media pages. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.02, 2-23-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER II. - ACCEPTABLE USE OF TECHNOLOGY SYSTEM 
 
Sec. 36.10. - Acceptable use. 
(a)  Personal use of technology must not interfere with the performance of assigned duties, must not have a detrimental effect on any city information technology system, and not be prohibited by this chapter. This includes the personal use of city-owned or managed technology that: 
(1)  Does not cause any additional expense to the city; 
(2)  Is infrequent and brief; 
(3)  Does not have a negative impact on overall user productivity; 
(4)  Does not interfere with the normal operations of the a user's department or work unit; 
(5)  Does not compromise the city in any way; 
(6)  Does not embarrass either the city or the user; 
(7)  Does not contravene other elements of this chapter; and 
(8)  Serves the interest of the city in allowing employees to address personal matters which cannot be addressed outside of work hours without leaving the workplace. 
(b)  Examples of personal communications that can be in the interest of the city include: 
(1)  Communications to alert household members about working late or other schedule changes; 
(2)  Communications to make alternative child care arrangements, communications with doctors, hospital staff or day care providers; 
(3)  Communications to determine the safety of family or household members, particularly in an emergency; 
(4)  Communications to reach businesses or governmental agencies that only can be contacted during work hours; and 
(5)  Communications to arrange emergency repairs to vehicles or residences. City departments may consult with the human resources department to determine whether a use is personal or business and, if the usage is personal, whether it is incidental. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.10, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.11. - Unacceptable use. 
The following activities are prohibited unless performed in the course of legitimate job responsibilities. The list below is by no means exhaustive, but provides a framework for activities which fall into the category of unacceptable uses of city IT systems. 
(1)  Engaging in any activity that is illegal under local, state and/or federal statutes as well as any activity that violates city policies and administrative directives; 
(2)  Accessing, displaying, storing or transmitting material that is offensive in nature, including sexually explicit materials, or any text or image that can be considered threatening, racially offensive, or hate speech. This includes any images, text, files, etc. sent via email to co-workers or outside parties. Accessing, storing, displaying, or transmitting pornographic materials using city-owned and managed technology is strictly forbidden; 
(3)  Engaging in any form of harassment, whether sexual or otherwise, or sending any unwelcome personal communication. It is the perception of the recipient that prevails in most instances, not the intent of the sender; 
(4)  Any personal use that interrupts city business and that keeps an employee from performing his work. Users should not use their city email account as a personal email address or to register with a non-work related social network. City systems shall also not be used to chat online, "blog," or shop online; 
(5)  Extensive personal use of the Internet for any non-work-related purpose during working hours which decreases the employees productivity or results in decreased performance of the city's Internet facilities; 
(6)  Violating any copyright, trade secret, patent and/or other intellectual property or similar laws or regulations, including, but not limited to, the installation or distribution of "pirated" or other software products that are not appropriately licensed for use by the city; 
(7)  Revealing a city account password to others or allowing use of a city account by others. This includes household members and visitors when work is being done at home. Revealing a city account password to an authorized technician during a troubleshooting procedure is not a violation of this chapter. In such a situation, a new password should be established as soon as possible, after the problem is resolved; 
(8)  Requesting a password to another users network or application account; 
(9)  Unauthorized reading, deleting, copying, modifying, printing and/or forwarding of electronic communications of another, or accessing electronic files of another without authorization; 
(10)  Unauthorized downloading or duplication of copyrighted material including, but not limited to, text and photographs from magazines, books or other copyrighted sources, copyrighted music and/or copyrighted movies. Downloading, copying, or installing copyrighted software for which the city or the end user does not have an active license is not permitted; 
(11)  Sending spam, chain letters, memes, and other non-city business related mass communications to either internal or external parties. Individual email accounts will be limited by technical controls as a preventive measure to detect Spam originating from a city email account. Large volume emails to recipients will not be allowed from individual email accounts. Request for approved email accounts designated for such business purposes will be submitted to the city manager; 
(12)  Approved email accounts must not regularly send bulk emails unless distribution lists are maintained. All undeliverable or invalid addresses from distribution lists must be regularly removed to prevent the city from not being able to send email through internet service providers and/or mail hosts; 
(13)  Downloading and/or copying music, photographs or video material, including such material that has been obtained legally, onto city computers or servers unless such are for authorized city purposes; 
(14)  Downloading and/or installing executable program files from external media or the Internet without the approval of the city manager or his designated official; 
(15)  Exporting software, technical information, encryption software and/or technology, in violation of international or regional export control laws; 
(16)  Using the city's electronic mail or Internet systems for private gain or profit; 
(17)  Using unauthorized personal software which allows peer-to-peer communications between two workstations (Yahoo Messenger, AIM, Google Talk, Torrent Networks, etc.); 
(18)  Maliciously introducing malware or similar programs into the network or server; 
(19)  All soliciting for political and/or religious causes as such are in violation of state and federal law, and/or other non-business uses not authorized by the city. Using city technology, electronic mail and/or Internet facilities for political activity including voting, private gain, gambling, shipping, games, entertainment or other non-business function unless permitted by this directive; 
(20)  Making fraudulent offers of products or services originating from any city account; 
(21)  Accessing any non-business related application which maintains a persistent application connection to the Internet, such as streaming videos or media, such as Pandora, YouTube, Netflix, and/or Google Video, among others; 
(22)  Including email "tag lines" or personal quotations other than ones that state the mission of the city or the user's department; 
(23)  Using the city's email system to automatically forward city email to a personal email account; 
(24)  Causing security breaches or disruptions of city communications. Security breaches or disruptions can include, but are not limited to: 
a.  Accessing data which the user is not authorized to access or logging into a server or user account that the user is not expressly authorized to access. 
b.  Causing network disruptions for malicious purposes including, but not limited to, network sniffing, ping floods, packet spoofing, denial of service of any kind, and forged routing information for malicious purposes. 
c.  Port scanning or vulnerability scanning for malicious purposes is prohibited. Non-malicious scanning that is part of a city-sanctioned security process is allowed. The city manager or ITSD should be notified prior to any such scanning. 
d.  Circumventing user authentication or security of any device, network or account. 
e.  Maliciously interfering with or denying service through a denial of service attack, or by other means. 
f.  Using any program/script/command, or sending messages of any kind, with the intent to interfere with, and/or disable, another user's device or session, via any means, locally or via the city's network. 
g.  Adding/removing hardware components, attaching external devices, and/or making configuration changes to information technology devices without the explicit approval by city manager or ITSD. 
h.  Storing confidential data on personally owned devices. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.11, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.12. - Fees associated with use of IT systems. 
The user of any device owned by the city or operated on the city's network that incurs an unauthorized fee or expenditure in excess of that approved by the city manager shall be responsible for reimbursement to the city for the actual charge incurred as well as any associated taxes, penalties, and fees associated therewith. This shall include overage fees for excessive minutes, text messages, and internet usage as applicable. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.12, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.13. - Monitoring to ensure compliance with usage policy. 
City systems may be monitored by the city to support operational, maintenance, auditing, security and/or investigative activities including enforcement of this chapter, legal requests, and public records requests or for other business purpose. Only department directors or higher may request monitoring of city administered IT systems for employees under their supervision for administrative purposes. Unauthorized monitoring or reading of electronic communications systems or their contents violates this chapter. Any request to monitor must be approved by the city manager or his designees or the city council. To obtain the necessary authorization, a written request from the requestor's department director to the city manager or city council must include subject employee information (i.e., name, employee number), a specific description of request (e.g., email, share drives, web usage, etc.) and name and phone number of the employee in the requesting department who is responsible for coordination of the request. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.13, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.14. - Electronic signatures and electronic records. 
(a)  Electronic signatures, an automated function that replaces a handwritten signature with a system-generated signature statement, and electronic records can be utilized as a means for authentication of city documents, computer generated city documents and/or electronic city entries among other uses. System-generated electronic signatures are considered legally binding as a means to identify the author of record for entries and confirm that the contents of what the author intended. City departments and staff will be allowed to utilize electronic signatures in accordance with this directive, city, state, and/or federal regulations regarding such. As such, acceptable use of electronic records and electronic signatures are allowed: 
(1)  Where policies, laws, regulations, and rules require a signature and that requirement is met if the document contains an electronic signature; 
(2)  Where policies, laws, regulations, and/or rules require a written document, and that requirement is met if the document is an electronic record; 
(3)  Each party to a transaction must agree to conduct the transaction electronically in order for the electronic transaction to be valid and binding. Consent may be implied from the circumstances, except with respect to any electronic records used to deliver information for which consumers are otherwise entitled by law to receive in paper or hardcopy form; 
(4)  If a law prohibits a transaction from occurring electronically, the transaction must occur in the manner specified by law; 
(5)  If a law requires an electronic signature to contain specific elements, the electronic signature must contain the elements specified by law; 
(6)  If a law requires that a record be retained, that requirement is satisfied by retaining an electronic record of the information in a record that accurately reflects the information set forth in the original record and shall remain accessible for later reference. When the requirements for retention require an original form, retention by an "electronic form" shall provide and satisfy the retention requirement. 
(b)  Procedures, forms, guidelines and resources for electronic signatures. 
(1)  Procedures for electronic signatures can be found under the Texas Uniform Electronic Transactions Act; 
(2)  United States governance can be found in 18 USC 2510 (Electronic Communications Privacy Act); 
(3)  Record management for the city is established by V.T.C.A., Local Government Code chs. 201 through 205. The state legislature requires local governments to establish a records program by ordinance; 
(4)  The city Charter mandates that the city secretary shall keep the records of the council and of the city. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.14, 2-23-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER III. - SECURITY REQUIREMENTS OF TECHNOLOGY SYSTEM 
 
Sec. 36.20. - Confidentiality of information on technological devices. 
Information stored on any city-administered information technology system should be classified in accordance with federal, state and local statues, ordinances, regulations, and/or policies among other directives regarding the confidentiality of the information. Users shall take the necessary steps or follow the prescribed processes to prevent unauthorized access to confidential information. Unclassified information should not be released to non-city entities without authorization and approval by the city manager's office. Users must comply with all city directives regarding use of information technology, including: 
(1)  Electronic communications (email, voice and Internet); 
(2)  Password management; 
(3)  Security; 
(4)  Data management and classification; 
(5)  Monitoring; 
(6)  Remote access. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.20, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.21. - Protection from unauthorized access. 
(a)  All personal computers, laptops, and workstations should be protected from unauthorized access when the system is unattended. The recommended method of security for city devices is with a password-protected screensaver (with the automatic activation feature set to 15 minutes or less) or by manually locking the device (Ctrl-Alt-Delete for most Microsoft operating systems). Devices that cannot be locked as described above should be secured by logging off the devices or turning them off. 
(b)  For all other technological devices, users must take reasonable and necessary precautions to secure and protect such devices; this includes requiring a password for access to mobile phones and tablets. 
(c)  ITSD regularly maintains operating systems, updates security software, and applies security patches by sending those updates during non-business hours to computers attached to the network. When a user leaves for the day, he should log off from his computer, but should leave the computer turned on and attached to the network. If laptops are secured during non-business hours and are not connected to the network, it is possible that updates were sent; as such, users should work with their business owner to ensure updates to portable devices are installed in a timely manner. 
(d)  All technology devices used by a technology user to connect to the city's networks shall continually execute approved security software with a current virus definition file. This includes user-owned equipment attached to the city's networks through remote access technologies. The city is not responsible for providing the required security software for user-owned computers. 
(e)  Email attachments that may constitute a risk to the city's technology environment will be removed from email messages passing through the city's mail servers if possible. Removed attachments are replaced by a message indicating that they have been removed and the header and text of the original message delivered normally. 
(f)  A spam message filter is used to reduce the transmission of chain letters, broadcast announcements, general advertisement postings, or any other message via email to a group of persons not requesting the message. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.21, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.22. - Passwords. 
(a)  Generally. Passwords are an important element of the acceptable use of technology and associated information security. A poorly chosen password may result in the compromise of the city's network. All technology users are responsible for taking appropriate steps to select and secure passwords. Users shall take reasonable and necessary care to prevent unauthorized access to workstations, laptops, applications, mobile and/or other devices. No departmental personnel, including administrative staff, shall request access to or maintain lists of other user passwords. 
(b)  Password guidelines. 
(1)  Use of "strong" passwords. Strong passwords that are at least eight characters in length, are not based on words in any language, slang, dialect or jargon, are not based on personal information such as family names, use at least one each English uppercase (A through Z), lowercase (a through z), digit (0 to 9) and non-alphanumeric character (!, $, #, %), are not common usage words like family, pets, friends, "Floresville," birthdays, phone numbers, addresses, computer terms, fantasy characters and/or common patterns like aaabbb, qwerty, zyxwvuts, 123321 or any derivation followed by a digit. 
(2)  If ITSD deems required, all users' passwords will expire at intervals of 90 days. In the event that this occurs, ITSD will institute a policy where users will be prompted to change passwords beginning ten days before the next expiration date. Passwords may not be re-used. 
(3)  Passwords will be changed immediately after a security breach has been detected to the affected city systems. 
(4)  As the city system software permits, an initial or reset password issued to a user will be valid only for the user's next log in. After that, the user must be prompted to change their password. 
(c)  Password protection guidelines. 
(1)  Do not write passwords down, store them online, or reveal them in any electronic format. 
(2)  Do not use the same password for city accounts as for other accounts (i.e., social media, personal email account, banking sites, etc.). 
(3)  Passwords must be treated as sensitive and confidential information; thus, do not share city passwords with anyone. 
(4)  ITSD support personnel may require a user's password to resolve a problem; however, the user shall be present to enter the required password. 
(5)  Do not talk about a password in the presence of others. 
(6)  Do not hint at the format of a password ("my family name"). 
(7)  Do not click on links in emails from unknown sources and provide account information that includes personal information and/or password. 
(8)  Do not reveal a password on questionnaires or security forms. 
(9)  Do not use the "remember password" feature. 
(10)  Do not store passwords in a file on any computer system without encryption. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.22, 2-23-2017)  
Sec. 36.23. - Reporting security breaches. 
Technology users shall report any suspected security violations or threat to the city manager and/or ITSD immediately. Any activity performed under a user ID/password combination is presumed to have been performed by that user and is the responsibility of that technology user. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.23, 2-23-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER IV. - RECORDS RETENTION OF TECHNOLOGY SYSTEM 
 
Sec. 36.30. - Records retention of electronic records. 
(a)  The city's approved declaration of compliance with the local government records retention schedules establishes record series and the retention period for each series. It is the content and function of an email, text message, or any other electronic communication that determines the retention period for that message. All email, text messages, or other electronic communication sent or received by a government is considered a government record. Therefore, all emails, text messages, and other electronic communications must be retained and disposed of according to the city's retention requirements. Email systems must meet the retention requirement found in Tex. Admin. Code ch. 7, § 7.77. 
(b)  Users and their supervisors or sponsor should seek guidance from the city manager if there is a question concerning whether an electronic message should be deleted. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.30, 2-23-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER V. - PENALTIES 
 
Sec. 36.40. - Penalties. 
Compliance with city administrative directives, security policies, and/or procedures is the responsibility of all city employees, contractors and/or other third parties. The city can temporarily or permanently suspend, block, and/or restrict access to information or physical assets, independent of such procedures, when it is reasonable and associated probable cause exists to do so in order to protect the confidentiality, integrity or availability of city resources as well as protect the city from liability, and/or to comply with applicable federal, state, and municipal laws, regulations, statutes, court orders, or other contractual obligations. Violations of any of portions of this chapter shall result in disciplinary actions in a manner as determined by the city manager. Disciplinary action may range from reprimand and loss of access privileges to suspension to separation of employment. Violations may also result in civil and/or criminal prosecution. 
(Ord. No. 2017-003, § 36.40, 2-23-2017)  
CHAPTER 37. - SOCIAL MEDIA USAGE POLICY  
SUBCHAPTER I. - APPLICATION OF POLICY 
 
Sec. 37.01. - Scope and purpose of policy. 
(a)  The purpose of the policy set forth in this chapter is to provide standards and procedures for the appropriate use of social media that is used in conducting city business. At present time this generally applies to the most popular sites, being Facebook, YouTube and Twitter; it is acknowledged that social media is an evolving communications tool and that new resources may become available over time. 
(b)  Except for posting to a city social media site, this chapter does not apply to use of social media by city employees that occurs on the employee's own time, or to use of social media that is not part of the employee's job. Such personal usage is covered under other applicable personnel policies and standards. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.01, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.02. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
City social media content means information posted or provided to a city social media site by a city employee (or authorized representative) when such activity is a part of the employee's job duties. 
City social media sites means those pages, sections or posting locations in social media websites that are established or maintained by an employee of the city who is authorized to do so as part of the employee's job, and that are used to conduct city business, communicate with officeholders or city staff, and/or communicate with or gather feedback from residents and other interested parties. 
Social media means a third-party website, desktop application, mobile application, or other form of technological communication which allows for the creation of content and dialogue around general content or a specific issue or area of interest. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.02, 2-9-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER II. - GENERAL GOVERNANCE OF SOCIAL MEDIA SITES 
 
Sec. 37.10. - General city approval of creation of social media sites. 
(a)  City social media sites may contain information that represents the city's position on policy issues and/or the positions of its leadership, or may create the appearance of representing such positions. For this reason, all city social media sites will be approved by the city manager in advance of creating the site. Those wishing to launch new city social media sites and/or pages should present his request to the city manager in writing with an explanation of why such site is necessary. All city social media sites are subject to review by the city council solely as applies to necessity of maintenance of such site. No city social media site will be approved without the designation of a specific departmental representative assigned responsibility for maintenance of the resource. 
(b)  The city manager or the city council may disable a city social media site or prohibit all posting of city social media content to a site at any time or for any reason, including, without limitation, any violation of any part of this chapter, unprofessional use of the resource, lack of use or disinterest by the public, or a department's failure to maintain the site. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.10, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.11. - Consolidated city social media sites. 
Unless a specific case is made and approved for a separate account, city social media content posted on social media sites should be coordinated through the city's central social media sites. A separate account may be approved if there is a limited, defined interest group for the targeted information (such as for the FEDC, 4a, P&Z, etc.). If approved, these accounts must be set up to "follow" all other city social media sites, if possible, and a designated social media representative must be selected to coordinate postings with the city manager and his social media representatives. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.11, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.12. - General posting procedures and management. 
Departments or programs should contact the city manager or his designated social media representatives to coordinate posts to the desired social media resource. To allow for after-hours or emergency use, login and password information for city social media sites shall be held by the city manager and his designated social media representatives. In the event of an emergency (water main break, disaster declaration, etc.), the city manager and his social media representative should be contacted as soon as possible to provide notice on city social media sites. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.12, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.13. - Following of other accounts. 
City social media site accounts shall only follow, friend, or otherwise appear to support official governmental or educational Twitter accounts, or accounts owned by an organization with an official partnership or supportive business relationship with a city department or program. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.13, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.14. - Login management. 
All city social media site login and password information, including those of boards and committees if authorized for separate social media accounts, will be shared with the city manager and his designated social media representatives. All login recovery emails must be official city email accounts. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.14, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.15. - General conduct of employees managing social media sites. 
Employees creating or posting information to a city social media site must conduct themselves at all times as representatives of the city and in accordance with all relevant human resources policies and administrative bulletins. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.15, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.16. - Scope and presentation of social media sites. 
(a)  City social media sites should be should be focused and limited in scope and topic, and should complement rather than replace the city's existing web resources. General "departmental" pages and associated content should be managed within the current city website. 
(b)  Information that is proprietary, attorney-client privileged, subject to state or federal privacy laws, and information not subject to disclosure under the Texas Public Information Act should not be posted on a city social media site. Any questions concerning this standard should be directed to the city manager. 
(c)  A clear statement of the intent, purpose and subject matter of the site, as well as a statement clearly articulating that all content and comments posted to the site are subject to public disclosure laws, should be clearly posted on any city social media site. 
(d)  All city social media sites shall clearly indicate the portion of the social media site that is maintained by the city and shall have appropriate city contact information prominently displayed. 
(e)  Links placed to a city social media site should link to a resource on http://www.floresvilletx.gov or other city-owned web site, a state, federal or local government site, an educational web site (.edu) or an organization with an official partnership or supportive business relationship with a city department or program. Exceptions to this rule will be at the discretion of the city manager, based on the relevance and appropriateness of the request. 
(f)  Design elements (logos, background, images) should be appropriate to the subject matter and consistent with the city's design guidelines. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.16, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.17. - Reporting security breaches. 
City social media site users shall report any suspected security violations or threat to the city manager immediately. Any social media activity performed on a social media site is presumed to have been performed by the city manager or his social media representatives, and responsibility for all posts lie with such individuals. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.17, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.18. - Passwords. 
(a)  Generally. Passwords are an important element of the acceptable use of social media and associated information security. A poorly chosen password may result in the compromise of the city's social media sites and managing individuals shall take reasonable and necessary care to prevent unauthorized access to city social media sites. 
(b)  Mandatory password guidelines. 
(1)  Use of "strong" passwords is mandatory for city social media sites. Unless disallowed by the social media site, it shall be required that the following rules shall apply: At least eight characters in length, are not based on words in any language, slang, dialect or jargon, are not based on personal information such as family names, use at least one each English uppercase (A through Z), lowercase (a through z), digit (0 to 9) and non-alphanumeric character (!, $, #, %), are not common usage words like family, pets, friends, "Floresville," birthdays, phone numbers, addresses, computer terms, fantasy characters and/or common patterns like aaabbb, qwerty, zyxwvuts, 123321 or any derivation followed by a digit. 
(2)  Passwords will be changed immediately after a security breach has been detected to the affected city social media site; 
(3)  The same password shall not be used for multiple city social media site accounts; 
(4)  Passwords must be treated as sensitive and confidential information and only shared with individuals authorized by the city manager; 
(5)  Do not click on links in emails from unknown sources and provide account information that includes personal information and/or password; 
(6)  Do not reveal a password on questionnaires or security forms; 
(7)  Do not use the "remember password" feature; 
(8)  Do not store passwords in a file on any computer system without encryption. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.18, 2-9-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER III. - PUBLIC COMMENTS ON SOCIAL MEDIA 
 
Sec. 37.20. - Setup of city social media sites regarding public comment. 
City social media site accounts must be set up in a way that either maximizes public comments or completely limits the resource to organizational postings only. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.20, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.21. - City social media sites open to the public. 
Membership to a city social media site should not be required in order for the public to post comments. If this is not possible, then a city email contact must be posted as an alternative for providing comments. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.21, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.22. - Disclaimer required and limited curating of content. 
A city department that creates a city social media site that permits interactivity and comments should provide a disclaimer on the site that posted comments do not necessarily reflect the views or position of the city. Editing or deleting of public comments posted on an "open forum" by the city or department that maintains the site is permitted if, and only if, the comments: 
(1)  Clearly violate the site's terms of service; 
(2)  Contain information about city business or operations that is confidential and non-public; 
(3)  Would reasonably be considered pornographic, obscene, or defamatory in nature; 
(4)  Directly promote or advocate violence or the threat of violence; 
(5)  Promote or advocate discrimination based on race, creed, color, age, religion, gender, marital status, national origin, physical or mental disability, or sexual orientation; 
(6)  Are solicitations of commerce or promotion of private business enterprises; 
(7)  Contain or link to inappropriate sexual content; 
(8)  Encourage or promote illegal activity; 
(9)  Include information that may compromise the safety or security of the public or public systems; or 
(10)  Appear to violate the legal ownership interest of any other party. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.22, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.23. - Solicitation of public media 
If photos, video, or other media are solicited through a city social media site, all submissions must be accepted and posted unless they fail to meet the guidelines as set forth in section 37.22. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.23, 2-9-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER IV. - STATE COMPLIANCE FOR SOCIAL MEDIA SITES 
 
Sec. 37.30. - Records retention of electronic records. 
The city's approved declaration of compliance with the local government records retention schedules establishes record series and the retention period for each series. Subject to these rules, all public comments and posted media files inclusive of any edited content must be archived and stored in accord with requirements of state and federal laws and city records retention policies. For city social media sites, the recommended course of action is to regularly (at least weekly) create a screenshot log of social media posts since the previous update. This recommended course of action may be superseded by another form of record retention that fulfills the requirements of retention of records. Prior to the removal of any postings on a city social media site, a screen shot or other archival record of the posting to be removed must be recorded. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.30, 2-9-2017)  
Sec. 37.31. - Open meetings interactions. 
Due to the potential for violations of V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 551 concerning open meetings requirements, individual members of the city council or any board subject to the Texas Open Meetings Act are prohibited from participating in postings or discussion threads on city social media sites created and maintained by the city. In addition, any use of city social media sites shall not serve as a replacement for postings and notifications required to be posted to city websites by state law. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.31, 2-9-2017)  
SUBCHAPTER V. - PENALTIES 
 
Sec. 37.40. - Penalties. 
Compliance with city administrative directives, security policies, and/or procedures is the responsibility of all city officials, employees, contractors and/or other third parties. The city can temporarily or permanently suspend, block, and/or restrict access to information or physical assets, independent of such procedures, when it is reasonable and associated probable cause exists to do so in order to protect the confidentiality, integrity or availability of city resources as well as protect the city from liability, and/or to comply with applicable federal, state, and municipal laws, regulations, statutes, court orders, or other contractual obligations. Violations of any of portions of this chapter shall result in disciplinary actions in a manner as determined by the city manager. Disciplinary action may range from reprimand and loss of access privileges to suspension to separation of employment. 
(Ord. No. 2017-002, § 37.40, 2-9-2017)  
CHAPTER 38. - ZONING BOARD OF ADJUSTMENT 
 
Sec. 38.01. - Created; composition; term, removal of members; filling of vacancies. 
There is hereby created and established a zoning board of adjustment, which shall consist of five members to be appointed by the city council. Such members shall serve for two-year staggered terms. The city council shall also appoint two alternate members of the zoning board of adjustment, any of which shall serve in the absence of one of the regular members when requested to do so by the city manager or the city manager's designee. The alternate members shall serve for two-year staggered terms. Both regular and alternate members may be removed from office for cause by the city council upon written charges and after a public hearing. Vacancies shall be filled for the unexpired term of any member or alternate member whose term becomes vacant. All cases to be heard by the zoning board of adjustment shall always be heard by a minimum number of four members. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(1), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.02. - Officers; compensation. 
(a)  The zoning board of adjustment shall meet and organize as soon as practicable and shall elect one of its members as chairperson. Such chairperson, or in his absence the acting chairperson, may administer oaths and compel the attendance of witnesses. 
(b)  The zoning board of adjustment shall serve without compensation. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(2), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.03. - Rules and meetings. 
The zoning board of adjustment shall adopt rules of procedure in accordance with the provisions of the city Charter and the city's ordinances not inconsistent with the provisions of V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 211.008 et seq. Meetings of the zoning board of adjustment shall be at such times as the zoning board of adjustment may determine. All meetings of the zoning board of adjustment shall be held in compliance with the Texas Open Meetings Act. The zoning board of adjustment shall keep minutes of its proceedings, showing the vote of each member upon each question or if absent or failing to vote, indicating such fact, and shall keep records of its examinations and other official actions, all of which shall be immediately filed in the office of the city secretary and shall be a public record. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(3), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.04. - Authority. 
(a)  The zoning board of adjustment may: 
(1)  Hear and decide an appeal that alleges error in an order, requirement, decision, or determination made by an administrative official in the enforcement of this chapter or an ordinance adopted under this chapter; 
(2)  Hear and decide special exceptions to the terms of a zoning ordinance when the ordinance requires the board to do so; 
(3)  Authorize in specific cases a variance from the terms of a zoning ordinance if the variance is not contrary to the public interest and, due to special conditions, a literal enforcement of the ordinance would result in unnecessary hardship, and so that the spirit of the ordinance is observed and substantial justice is done; and 
(4)  Hear and decide other matters authorized by an ordinance adopted under the city's zoning regulations. 
(b)  In exercising its authority under subsection (a)(1) of this section, the board may reverse or affirm, in whole or in part, or modify the administrative official's order, requirement, decision, or determination from which an appeal is taken and make the correct order, requirement, decision, or determination, and for that purpose the board has the same authority as the administrative official. 
(c)  The concurring vote of 75 percent of the members of the board is necessary to: 
(1)  Reverse an order, requirement, decision, or determination of an administrative official; 
(2)  Decide in favor of an applicant on a matter on which the board is required to pass under a zoning ordinance; or 
(3)  Authorize a variation from the terms of a zoning ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(4), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.05. - Appeals. 
(a)  Any of the following persons may appeal to the zoning board of adjustment a decision made by an administrative official under the city's zoning regulations: 
(1)  A person aggrieved by the decision; or 
(2)  Any officer, department, board, or bureau of the municipality affected by the decision. 
(b)  The appellant must file with the board and the official from whom the appeal is taken a notice of appeal specifying the grounds for the appeal. The appeal must be filed within a reasonable time as determined by the rules of the board. On receiving the notice, the official from whom the appeal is taken shall immediately transmit to the board all the papers constituting the record of the action that is appealed. 
(c)  An appeal stays all proceedings in furtherance of the action that is appealed unless the official from whom the appeal is taken certifies in writing to the board facts supporting the official's opinion that a stay would cause imminent peril to life or property. In that case, the proceedings may be stayed only by a restraining order granted by the board or a court of record on application, after notice to the official, if due cause is shown. 
(d)  The board shall set a reasonable time for the appeal hearing and shall give public notice of the hearing and due notice to the parties in interest. A party may appear at the appeal hearing in person or by agent or attorney. The board shall decide the appeal within a reasonable time. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(5), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.06. - Special exceptions and variances. 
(a)  All applications for special exceptions shall be in writing and shall specify the facts involved, the relief desired, the provision this Code authorizing the special exception, and the grounds therefor. 
(b)  Each such application shall be filed with the community development department which, after investigation, shall transmit such application together with their report to the zoning board of adjustment within 15 business days after the filing of the application with the administrative officer. A fee, as specified on the schedule of fees on file in the office of the city secretary, must accompany all applications for said special exceptions and variances. 
(c)  The zoning board of adjustment shall fix a reasonable time for the hearing of all applications for special exceptions and variances, give due notice to the parties in interest, and decide the same within a reasonable time. Upon the hearing, any party may appear in person or by an agent or by attorney. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(6), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.07. - Limitation on special exceptions and variances. 
Any special exception or variance authorized by the zoning board of adjustment shall constitute authority to authorize the issuance of a zoning permit or a certificate of occupancy, as the case may be, if applied for within 120 days from the date of favorable action on the part of the zoning board of adjustment, unless such zoning board of adjustment authorizes a longer period. If the zoning permit or certificate of occupancy shall not have been applied for within such 120 days, or such extended period as the zoning board of adjustment may have authorized, then the grant of the special exception or variance shall terminate. Such termination shall be without prejudice to a subsequent application to the zoning board of adjustment in accordance with the rules and regulations regarding applications. No application to the zoning board of adjustment shall be allowed on the same piece of property prior to the expiration of six months from a ruling of the zoning board of adjustment on any application to such body unless other property in the same block or within 500 feet thereof, within such six-month period, has been altered or changed by a ruling of the zoning board of adjustment, in which case such change of circumstances shall permit the allowance of such an application but shall in nowise have any force in law to compel the zoning board of adjustment, after a hearing, to grant such subsequent application, but such application shall be considered on its merits as in all other cases. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(8), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.08. - Appeals. 
Any person, jointly or severally, aggrieved by any decision of the zoning board of adjustment, or any taxpayer, or any officer, department, board or bureau of the city, may present to a court of record a petition for a writ of certiorari, as provided by V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 211.011, duly verified setting forth that such decision is illegal, in whole or in part, specifying the grounds of the illegality. Such petition shall be presented to the court within ten days after the filing of the decision in the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(9), 11-9-2017)  
Sec. 38.09. - Enforcement; remedies. 
If a building or other structure is erected, constructed, reconstructed, altered, repaired, converted, or maintained or if a building, other structure, or land is used in violation of this chapter, the city attorney, upon approval by the city council, in addition to other remedies, may institute appropriate action to: 
(1)  Prevent the unlawful erection, construction, reconstruction, alteration, repair, conversion, maintenance, or use; 
(2)  Restrain, correct, or abate the violation; 
(3)  Prevent the occupancy of the building, structure, or land; or 
(4)  Prevent any illegal act, conduct, business, or use on or about the premises. 
(Ord. No. 2017-027, § II(10), 11-9-2017)  
Title V - PUBLIC WORKS  
CHAPTER 50. - PUBLIC UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference— Public utilities, § 2.06; sales of electricity, water and sewer services, § 2.15; franchise and public utilities, § X. 
State Law reference— Municipal utility systems, general powers, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 551 et seq. 
 
SUBCHAPTER I. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
Sec. 50.01. - Utility easements. 
(a)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Utility easement means an interest in land granted to the city for installing and maintaining utilities across, over, or under private land together with the right to enter thereon with machinery and other vehicles necessary for the maintenance of said utilities. 
(b)  If the owner of the property upon which the utility easement is located desires to use it for lawn purposes, fencing across the easement shall be permitted, but gates along the side lot lines must be provided. The gates shall be 15 feet wide (two seven-foot gates) and shall be capable of being opened and closed at all times. These gates shall be secured in the center by a drop rod or some similar device which does not obstruct free passage over the easement. The drop rod may be lowered into a drop rod keeper, installed so as to be flush with the ground level. No permanent-type center pole for the gates may be erected on the easement. The gates provided for herein shall remain unlocked at all times. 
(c)  Maintenance of the easement shall be the responsibility of the owner of the property upon which it is located. It shall be the duty of the property owner to keep the area across, over, or under this easement clear of any structure, debris, vegetation, trees, shrubs, or landscaping whatsoever except that lawn grass which shall be regularly mowed and controlled may be grown thereon. 
(Code 1996, § 50.01; Ord. No. 0009, 2-4-1971)  
SUBCHAPTER II. - UTILITY BILLING PROCEDURE 
 
Sec. 50.15. - Method of billing. 
It is hereby provided that monthly charges for water service, sewer service, and garbage disposal service shall be made to each customer therefor on one monthly statement. Such statement shall show the monthly charge for each service separately and the total for all three services combined, together with any other pertinent data in line with existing practice. 
(Code 1996, § 50.15; Ord. No. 0049, 9-3-1970)  
Sec. 50.16. - Payment procedure; delinquency; discontinuance of water service. 
(a)  It is hereby provided that each customer shall be required to pay the total charge for all three said services for each month for which the customer is billed, and that no payment less than the full amount due for all three said services for each of such months, as shown by each of such statements shall be accepted by the city. Failure to pay the full total due as shown on each such statement, shall constitute a delinquent account and constitute an express refusal to pay for each of said three services, whether considered separately or collectively. 
(b)  All such combined statements of account shall be payable on the first day of each calendar month for the charges for such three services for the preceding billing month. No discounts shall be allowed after the tenth day of the month in which such statement is rendered. Water services shall be discontinued to any connection on which the full combined statement shall not have been paid on or before the 20th day of the month in which such statement was rendered, in accordance with the procedure set forth in section 50.17. 
(Code 1996, § 50.16; Ord. No. 0049, 9-3-1970)  
Sec. 50.17. - Disconnection for late payment. 
(a)  It is the policy of the city to discontinue utility service to customers by reason of nonpayment of bills only after notice and a meaningful opportunity to be heard on disputed bills. The city's form for application for utility service and all bills shall contain, in addition to the title, address, room number, and telephone number of the official in charge of billing, clearly visible and easily readable provisions to the effect: 
(1)  That all bills are due and payable on or before the date set forth on the bill; 
(2)  That if any bill is not paid by or before that date, a second bill will be mailed containing a cutoff notice that if the bill is not paid within ten days of the mailing of the second bill, service will be discontinued for nonpayment; and 
(3)  That any customer disputing the correctness of his bill shall have a right to a hearing at which time he may be represented in person and by counsel or any other person of his choosing and may present orally or in writing his complaint and contentions to the city official in charge of utility billing. This official shall be authorized to order that the customer's service not be discontinued and shall have the authority to make a final determination of the customer's complaint. 
(b)  Requests for delays or waiver of payment will not be entertained; only questions of proper and correct billing will be considered. In the absence of payment of the bill rendered or resort to the hearing procedure provided herein, service will be discontinued at the time specified, but in no event until the charges have been due and unpaid for at least 30 days. 
(c)  When it becomes necessary for the city to discontinue utility service to a customer for nonpayment of bills, service will be reinstated only after all bills for service then due have been paid, along with a turn-on charge in the sum as currently established or as hereafter adopted by ordinance of the city council from time to time, and kept on file in the office of the city secretary. 
(Code 1996, § 50.17)  
CHAPTER 51. - SOLID WASTE COLLECTION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Charter reference— Garbage disposal, § 2.08. 
State Law reference— Minimum standards of sanitation and health protection measures, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 341; local regulation of sanitation, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 342; Solid Waste Disposal Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 361; municipal solid waste, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 363; litter, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 365. 
 
Sec. 51.01. - Franchise. 
The full text of the franchise agreement for solid waste collection and/or contract for solid waste collection and disposal is available in the office of the city secretary. 
(Ord. No. 2017-012, § 51.01, 7-13-2017)  
Sec. 51.02. - Mandatory service. 
All residents, including businesses, are required to use the solid waste collection services of the franchisee approved by the city. 
(Ord. No. 2017-012, § 51.02, 7-13-2017)  
Sec. 51.03. - Enforcement. 
The franchisee may enforce such terms and conditions of the franchise agreement for solid waste collection and/or contract for solid waste collection and disposal, as may be amended from time to time. 
(Ord. No. 2017-012, § 51.03, 7-13-2017)  
Sec. 51.04. - Service and fees.
