(1)  All persons, or sole individuals, who are not eligible for an initial permit under section 117.03 on the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived, but who desire to obtain a permit when the opportunity to do so becomes available, shall register with the city code enforcement department and be placed on a single waiting list by preparing the appropriate forms required by the city's code compliance department. 
(2)  The city shall create and maintain one waiting list. This waiting list shall be for resident applicants and for nonresident applicants. A place on this waiting list for permits is on a first-come, first served basis. 
(3)  The total number of location licenses issued to residents and nonresidents is as defined in section 117.02. 
(4)  The waiting list shall be comprised of the business owner or sole individual that will hold the location license, and shall not differ from that person. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 4, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 4)  
Sec. 117.05. - Business location restrictions and relocation requirements. 
(a)  The city may not issue a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine location license for use within 1,500 feet from door entry of business to property line of the following: 
(1)  All places of education or higher learning, to include pre-school facilities, child day care, elementary, middle or intermediate schools, high schools, places of higher learning colleges, technical schools or universities; 
(2)  Hospitals or places where medical attention is received or pharmaceuticals are dispensed, to include pharmacies, clinics, night clinics, adult day care, veteran hospitals, hospitals, major trauma units, or where ambulatory services are stationed; 
(3)  Any place of religious worship, to include any established building of gathering for worship, to include, but not be limited to, a building of a denomination or other location where a group of people (a congregation) comes to perform acts of religious praise, honor, or devotion; 
(4)  Any city, county, school district, or other property owned or operated by a political subdivision of the state or the federal government; or 
(5)  Any location where children congregate, to include, but not be limited to, playgrounds, parks, city maintained swimming pools, restaurants or eateries that facilitate a playground area or day care centers. 
(b)  In accordance with city zoning ordinances, the city may only issue a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine location license in zoned areas as follows: a commercial or industrial zone. 
(c)  There shall be required to be an amount of parking spaces for each location as calculated under the ordinances of the city for commercial property locations. 
(d)  Relocation of premises. Active business permit holders who wish to relocate the licensed establishment for which they are permitted to another location must notify the city's code compliance department immediately and receive an amended permit prior to relocating. Upon immediate notice to the city's code compliance department, the business owner shall be allowed 45 days to move all operations to new location. The 45 days shall commence at 12:00 midnight on the same day after notice was received, and shall continue to 12:00 midnight on the 45th day. The city reserves the right to deny the relocation in the event that it finds significant negative impact for the surrounding properties or is a violation of this subsection (a) or (b) of this section. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 5, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 5)  
Sec. 117.06. - Issuance of permits and licenses. 
The following section shall apply specifically to all skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine locations in accordance with this chapter as well as state and federal laws. Those skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machines herein not specifically mentioned are not exempt from state and federal laws as applied to tax fees. 
(1)  Every location which owns, controls, possesses, exhibits, or displays any skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine, shall require a location license issued by the city in accordance with this chapter. 
(2)  Every owner hereinabove, who owns, controls, possesses, exhibits, displays, or who permits to be exhibited or displayed in the city any skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine, shall pay and there is hereby levied on every coin-operated and/or slot machine as defined in this chapter, except such as are exempted herein, an annual permit fee as set forth in section 117.03. 
(3)  All permits for skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machines are payable annually in advance. Prior to the placement by an owner of a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine, there shall be attached or affixed thereto a valid permit for the machine. 
(4)  Machines defined in this chapter as skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machines, capable of independent operation with separate activating coin mechanisms whether placed separately or in series and regardless of any electrical mechanical or manual component, shall be considered separate machines in regard to permitting. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 6, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 6)  
Sec. 117.07. - Replacement of lost, stolen and destroyed valid permits. 
The city shall not make a cash refund of the permit fee paid on any skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine. The city shall provide a duplicate permit if a valid permit has been lost, stolen, or destroyed. The fee for each duplicate permit is as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time. An original permit for which a duplicate permit has been issued is void. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 7, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 7)  
Sec. 117.08. - Registration of machines. 
Each skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine shall be registered with the city by make, type and serial number. A permit issued by the city or state shall be affixed to each such registered machine. Each skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine shall have a serial number, which is clearly visible on the outside surface of the machine. If a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine is not manufactured with a serial number, an owner shall assign a serial number to the machine and either stamp or engrave the assigned number on the machine. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 8, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 8)  
Sec. 117.09. - Attachment of permits to coin-operated machines. 
A permit shall be securely affixed to any permanent surface of a machine in such a manner that the permit may be clearly seen by the public. A permit issued for a certain skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine shall not be transferred to another machine. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 9, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 9)  
Sec. 117.10. - Sealing of machines. 
(a)  The city may seal any skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine on which the initial premises permit fee or the yearly renewal premises permit fee has not been paid. The city shall charge an administrative fee as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time for the release of any machine sealed as provided herein for nonpayment of fees. It shall be unlawful for any person to break the seal affixed in the name of the city or exhibit, display, or remove from location any machine on which the seal has been broken. 
(b)  Every skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine subject to the payment of the fees levied in this chapter, and upon which the fee has not been paid as provided herein, is herby declared to be a public nuisance, and the business displaying said machines may be denied operation by the city, as well as denying the continued operation of said business. All permits allowing said business, as referred to in this chapter, to operate may be denied and/or discontinued. 
(c)  Upon proof that all fees have been paid in full and an inspection of the location of business has been completed any and/or all sealed machines may be unsealed by the code compliance department, police department or their designees. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 10, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 10)  
Sec. 117.11. - Existing laws and inspections. 
(a)  Nothing herein shall be construed or have the effect to license, permit, authorize or legalize any machine, device, table or coin-operated or slot machine, the keeping, exhibition, operation, display or maintenance of which is now illegal or in violation of any article of the penal code of the state and of any federal laws of the United States of America. 
(b)  "Gambling devices," as defined by V.T.C.A., Penal Code ch. 47, and as interpreted by judicial decision (Hardy v. State, No 01-0779, Tex. 2003 and One Super Cherry Master Video 8-Liner Machine v. State, No. 01-0673, Tex. 2003), are prohibited from use as coin-operated or slot machines or any machine for which a permit may be lawfully issued. 
(c)  In addition to any other penalty or punishment imposed by law, violation of this chapter shall be cause for revocation of a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine location license issued pursuant to this chapter. The city reserves the right to inspect the premises of any skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine business establishment in order to investigate compliance with this chapter. The owner of a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine business or their employees shall not prohibit city inspectors, police or fire personnel, at any time, to enter the premise of operation of the permit to ensure there are no violations of city, state or federal laws to include correct machine count issued to the permit, correct licenses or permits per machine, fire code violations or penal code violations. The entries and exits shall be maintained as to allow unobstructed, unregulated, free entry into said location by inspectors, police or fire personnel without any delay of entry. Any violations of this section shall be considered a violation of this chapter and will be considered grounds for revocation. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 11, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 11)  
Sec. 117.12. - Violations. 
(a)  Any person, business owner, manager violating any provision of this chapter shall, upon conviction of such violation, be deemed guilty of a Class C misdemeanor. The unlawful operation of any single skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine shall constitute a distinct and separate offense for each day that the same is operated, or exhibited and is punishable by a fine not to exceed that as set forth in this section. In addition to any other penalty or punishment imposed by law, violation of this section shall be cause for revocation of a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine premises permit issued pursuant to this chapter. 
(b)  The city council, or its designees, reserves the right to revoke any location license or permit to maintain and operate a skill or pleasure coin-operated or slot machine business of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2015-033, § 12, 12-10-2015; Ord. of 1-11-2016, § 12)  
Title XIII - GENERAL PROVISIONS  
CHAPTER 130. - GENERAL OFFENSES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference— V.T.C.A., Penal Code ch. 1 et seq. 
 
SUBCHAPTER I. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
Sec. 130.01. - Loitering; window peeping prohibited. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter on any private property situated within the city limits without the consent of the owner of such property. 
(b)  Definitions. The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this subchapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Loiter means the action of a person who shall remain at any given location without having any legitimate business at that location for an unreasonable length of time. 
Owner means any person in lawful possession of the property or dwelling house involved. 
(b)  The chief of police and his deputies, and any other duly authorized peace officer acting under county or state authority is hereby empowered to arrest any person suspected of loitering on private property. 
(c)  It shall be unlawful for any person to look, peer, or peep into, or be found loitering around, or within view of any window not on his own property, with the intent of looking through such window in such a manner as would be likely to interfere with the occupants reasonable expectation of privacy without the occupant's express or implied consent. 
(Code 1996, § 130.02; Ord. No. 0027, 8-4-1960)  
Sec. 130.02. - Cutting across private property. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to cross over or through in an automobile or other vehicle public or private real property in the city without the consent of the owner, proprietor, occupant, lessee, or agent in charge of such property unless such passage be made upon the right-of-way of a public road, or a private right-of-way, and in such case the person shall first receive the permission of the owner, proprietor, occupant, lessee, or agent in charge of such private right-of-way. 
(Code 1996, § 130.03; Ord. No. 0023, 12-19-1973)  
Sec. 130.03. - Hunting. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to take, kill, wound, shoot at, or hunt any wild game animal or wild game bird, or for that matter, any bird or fowl within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1996, § 130.04; Ord. No. 0023, 12-19-1973) 
State Law reference— V.T.C.A., Parks and Wildlife Code ch. 1 et seq.  
Sec. 130.04. - Discharge of firearms or fireworks. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to discharge any type of firearm within the corporate limits of the city except at an approved shooting range. It shall also be unlawful for any person to sell, possess, discharge, ignite or explode any fireworks within the corporate limits of the city except as part of an city-approved public display. Fireworks shall include sparklers. 
(Code 1996, § 130.05; Ord. No. 0023, 12-19-1973) 
State Law reference— Authority of municipality to regulate the discharge of firearms, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 229.001 et seq.; authority of municipality to regulate the use of fireworks, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 342.003; state law does not preempt municipal authority to prohibit or regulate use of fireworks, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.004; regulation of fireworks and fireworks displays, V.T.C.A., Occupations Code § 2154.001 et seq.; fireworks use, displays and regulations, 28 Tex. Admin. Code § 34.801 et seq.  
SUBCHAPTER II. - CURFEW FOR MINORS 
 
Sec. 130.20. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this subchapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Consent means actual consent by a parent to the minor's presence in public as provided in this subchapter. 
Knowledge means knowledge that the minor is not at home and that the minor is not under the adequate supervision of another responsible adult. It need not be acknowledged that the minor is in any particular place at any particular time, but rather solely knowledge that the minor is unsupervised. 
Minor means anyone under the age of 16 other than a minor who has had his disabilities removed for general purposes or a person under the age of 16 who is legally married. 
Parent means any adult having the legal or actual responsibility for the care, custody, and control of a minor, including the natural parent, the managing conservator, the joint managing conservator, the possessory conservator, a non-parent managing conservator, joint managing conservator, or possessory conservator, a grandparent with established access rights, a legal guardian of the person of a minor, or an authorized agent of any of the above. In this regard, a parent is any person who has a legal right to possession of the child greater than that of the general public at the time of the offense charged. 
Public place means any location within the city limits other than a private home or the appurtenances of a private home (such as porch or driveway) of the parent of the minor. The term "public place" expressly includes any road, street, highway, parking lot, or other location for vehicle traffic upon which any vehicle (including a truck) is traveling without any parent of the minor in the automobile. 
(Code 1996, § 130.20; Ord. No. 0022, 1-27-1983; Ord. No. 203, 6-12-2003; Ord. No. 244, 4-12-2007; Ord. No. 2014-007, § 130.20, 5-21-2014; Ord. No. 2018-003, § 130.20, 2-22-2018)  
Sec. 130.21. - Curfew imposed. 
(a)  Established. It shall be unlawful for any minor to be present in any public place between the hours of 11:00 p.m. and 5:00 a.m. without the actual presence of a parent (which term includes the authorized agent of a parent) of the minor. 
(b)  Defenses. It is a defense to prosecution of this section that the minor was: 
(1)  Accompanied by another minor whose parent was present; 
(2)  In a motor vehicle with another minor whose parent was present; 
(3)  Engaged in any employment activity, official school activity, at a public school and pursuant to any school activities, or going to or from any employment or school activity without any detour or stop; 
(4)  Involved in an emergency; 
(5)  Attending any official school, religious, or other recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by any civic organization, political organization, or religious organization, or going to or returning home from any such activity; 
(6)  Engaged in exercising their rights under the United States Constitution providing for the free exercise of religion, freedom of speech, right of assembly, or petition to the government; 
(7)  Engaged in an errand for the minor's parent and continuing on such errand without detour or unnecessary stopping. 
(c)  Negligent supervision. It shall be a defense to prosecution for the minor that the minor was unable to obtain transportation from an event ending after 11:00 p.m. where a parent (which term includes the authorized agent of a parent) had obligated himself or herself to retrieve the child at the appointed time but failed to appear, and the minor was continuing home without detour or unnecessary stopping. The obligated parent shall be subject to the provisions of section 130.23. 
(Code 1996, § 130.21; Ord. No. 203, 6-12-2003; Ord. No. 244, 4-12-2007; Ord. No. 2014-007, § 130.21, 5-21-2014; Ord. No. 2018-003, § 130.21, 2-22-2018)  
Sec. 130.22. - Enforcement. 
(a)  In the event that any minor be found in a public place during prohibited hours as provided for in section 130.21, the minor shall be transported by the law enforcement officer to a secure place (which may include the minor's home). If the law enforcement officer is unable to locate a parent of the minor, or if no parent of the minor is willing to take responsibility for the minor, the officer shall, as appropriate, deliver the minor into the custody of: 
(1)  A child protective service worker with the state department of protective and regulatory services; 
(2)  A juvenile probation officer; or 
(3)  Any other suitable adult whom the officer deems appropriate. 
(b)  At the time of the release of the minor to one of the individuals named above, the officer shall cite the minor for a violation of this subchapter. 
(Code 1996, § 130.22; Ord. No. 0022, 1-27-1983; Ord. No. 203, 6-12-2003; Ord. No. 244, 4-12-2007; Ord. No. 2014-007, § 130.22, 5-21-2014; Ord. No. 2018-003, § 130.22, 2-22-2018)  
Sec. 130.23. - Negligent supervision. 
(a)  Any parent who shall knowingly permit a minor to remain in a public place during prohibited hours without the parent providing adequate supervision for the minor shall be guilty of a Class C misdemeanor. 
(b)  Any parent who shall otherwise allow a minor to remain in a public place during prohibited hours without the parent providing adequate supervision for the minor shall be issued a warning for the first such occurrence. Any subsequent occurrence shall result in the parent being guilty of a Class C misdemeanor. 
(Code 1996, § 130.23; Ord. No. 0022, 1-27-1983; Ord. No. 203, 6-12-2003; Ord. No. 244, 4-12-2007; Ord. No. 2014-007, § 130.22, 5-21-2014; Ord. No. 2018-003, § 130.23, 2-22-2018)  
Sec. 130.24. - Review period. 
In accordance with V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 370.002, the ordinance from which this subchapter is derived shall be reviewed at a public hearing no later than the third anniversary of the effective date of said ordinance, and before every third anniversary thereafter. At such hearing, the ordinance's effect on the community shall be taken into consideration, and a determination shall be made by the city council on whether to abolish, continue, or modify the ordinance from which this subchapter is derived. 
(Ord. No. 2014-007, § 130.24, 5-21-2014; Ord. No. 2018-003, § 130.24, 2-22-2018)  
CHAPTER 131. - LITTERING[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Texas Litter Abatement Act, V.T.C.A., Health and Safety Code ch. 365. 
 
Sec. 131.01. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Aircraft means any contrivance now known or hereafter invented, used, or designed for navigation or for flight in the air. The term "aircraft" includes helicopters and lighter-than-air powered craft and balloons. 
Authorized private receptacle means a container of watertight construction with a tight fitting lid or cover capable of preventing the escape of contents within. Such receptacles shall have handles or other means for safe and convenient handling and be of such size or sufficient capacity to hold all litter generated between collections and shall be in compliance with the regulations promulgated. 
Construction site means any private or public property upon which repairs to existing buildings, construction of new buildings, or demolition of existing structures is taking place. 
Handbill means any printed or written matter, any sample or device, dodger, circular, leaflet, pamphlet, paper, booklet, or any other printed matter of literature which is not delivered by United States mail. 
Litter means: 
(1)  Decayable waste from a public or private establishment, residence, or restaurant, including animal and vegetable waste material from a market or storage facility handling or storing produce or other food products, or the handling, preparation, cooking, or consumption of food, but not including sewage, body wastes, or industrial by-products; or 
(2)  Nondecayable solid waste, except ashes, that consists of: 
a.  Combustible waste material, including paper, rags, cartons, wood, excelsior, furniture, rubber, plastics, yard trimmings, leaves, or similar materials; 
b.  Noncombustible waste material, including glass, crockery, tin or aluminum cans, metal furniture, and similar materials that do not burn at ordinary incinerator temperatures of 1,800 degrees Fahrenheit or less; and 
c.  Discarded or worn-out manufactured materials and machinery, including motor vehicles and parts of motor vehicles, tires, aircraft, farm implements, building or construction materials, appliances, and scrap metal. 
Loading and unloading dock means any dock space or area used by any moving vehicle for the purpose of receiving, shipping, and transporting goods, wares, commodities, and persons located on or adjacent to any stream, river, or land. 
Private premises means all property, including, but not limited to, vacant land or any land, building, or other structure designed or used for residential, commercial, business, industrial, institutional, or religious purposes, together with any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, fence, porch, steps, vestibule, mailbox, and other structure appurtenant thereto. 
Public place means any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys, or other public ways, lakes, rivers, watercourses, or fountains and any and all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds, and buildings. 
Public receptacles means any receptacles provided by or authorized by the city. 
Vehicle means every device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon land or water, including devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
(Code 1996, § 131.01; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.02. - Littering; unlawful deposit of waste prohibited. 
(a)  No person shall deposit any litter within the city except in public receptacles, in authorized private receptacles for collection or in any duly licensed disposal facility. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to place or dispose of in any manner any litter along or near or on any land adjoining any public road or highway or ditch except in a properly maintained landfill operated by the city or licensed by the city council. 
(Code 1996, § 131.02; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.03. - Prevention of scattering. 
Persons placing litter in public receptacles or in authorized private receptacles shall do so in such manner as to prevent litter from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any public place or private premises. 
(Code 1996, § 131.03; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.04. - Upsetting or tampering with receptacles. 
No person shall upset or tamper with a public or private receptacle designed or used for the deposit of litter or cause or permit its contents to be deposited or strewn in or upon any public place or private premises. 
(Code 1996, § 131.04; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.05. - Sidewalks and alleys to be kept clear. 
The person owning, occupying, or in control of any public place or private premises shall keep the sidewalks and alleys adjacent thereto free of litter. 
(Code 1996, § 131.05; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.06. - Owner to maintain private premises. 
(a)  The owner or person in control of any private premises shall at all times maintain the premises free of litter. 
(b)  The owner or person in control of private premises shall, if public receptacles are unavailable, maintain authorized private receptacles for collection in such a manner that litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any public place or private premises. 
(Code 1996, § 131.06; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.07. - Littering from vehicles or aircraft. 
(a)  No person, while the operator of or passenger in a vehicle, shall deposit litter upon any public place or private premises. 
(b)  No person shall drive or move any loaded or partly loaded truck or other vehicle within the city unless such vehicle is so constructed or loaded as to prevent any part of its load, contents, or litter from being blown or deposited upon any public place or private premises. Nor shall any person drive or move any vehicle or truck within the city, the wheels or tires of which carry onto or deposit in any public place or private premises, mud, dirt, sticky substances, litter, or foreign matter of any kind. 
(c)  No person shall transport junk, refuse, or garbage in any manner over and upon any street, alley, road, parkway, park drive, or public highway in such a manner that it is strewn upon and along such street, alley, road, or public highway. 
(d)  No person in any aircraft shall throw out, drop, or deposit any litter within the city. 
(Code 1996, § 131.07; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.08. - Litter in parks. 
No person shall deposit litter in any park within the city except in receptacles and in such a manner that the litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any part of the park or upon any other public place or private premises. Where receptacles are not provided, all such litter shall be removed from the park by the person responsible for its presence and properly disposed of elsewhere in a lawful manner. 
(Code 1996, § 131.08; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.09. - Litter at construction sites; loading and unloading docks. 
(a)  Each contractor shall be responsible for the job site so that litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any public place or other private premises. 
(b)  Litter or other debris, including dirt and mud, deposited as the result of normal construction process upon any public place or private premises, shall be removed by the contractor. 
(c)  The person owning, operating or in control of a loading or unloading dock shall maintain private receptacles for collection of litter, and shall at all times maintain the dock area free of litter in such a manner that litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any public place or other private premises. 
(Code 1996, § 131.09; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.10. - Parking lots. 
(a)  Litter receptacles required. Any public place or private premises containing any provision for parking vehicles shall be equipped with litter receptacles in compliance with this section. Such premises shall include, but not be limited to, such places as shopping centers, outdoor theaters, drive-in restaurants, gasoline service stations, apartment developments, parking lots, and any other place where provision is made for vehicles to stop or park in a designated area for any purpose. 
(b)  Number of receptacles. All premises having parking lots shall provide in an easily accessible location, a minimum of one refuse container for every 50 parking spaces. 
(c)  Specifications. Litter receptacles shall have tight fitting lids or tops and shall be weighted or attached to the ground or other fixed structures as necessary to prevent spillage. A minimum container size of 20 gallons or 75.7 liters shall be used. 
(d)  Cleanliness. Premises used for the purpose designated herein shall be kept in a litter-free condition and all litter shall be removed periodically from the receptacles. 
(e)  Obligation to use receptacles. It shall be the duty and obligation of all persons using parking areas to use such litter receptacles as hereinabove provided for the purposes intended and it shall be unlawful for any person to deposit upon any such parking lot any litter. 
(Code 1996, § 131.10; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.11. - Distribution of handbills. 
(a)  Public places. No person shall deposit or sell any handbill in or upon any public place provided, however, that it shall not be unlawful on any public place for any person to hand out or distribute without charge to the receiver, any handbill to any person willing to accept it. 
(b)  Private premises. 
(1)  Regulation. No person shall deposit or unlawfully distribute any handbill in or upon private premises, except by handing or transmitting any such handbill directly to the occupant of such private premises, provided, however, that in case of private premises which are not posted against the receiving of handbills or similar material, such person, unless requested by anyone upon such premises not to do so may securely place any such handbill in such a manner as to prevent such handbill from being deposited by the elements upon any public place or other private premises, except mailboxes may not be so used when prohibited by federal postal law or regulations. 
(2)  Exemption for newspapers and political literature. The provisions of this section shall not apply to the distribution upon private premises only of newspapers or political literature; except that newspapers and political literature shall be placed in such a manner as to prevent their being carried or deposited by the elements upon any public place or other private premises. 
(c)  Placing handbills on vehicles. No person shall deposit any handbill in or upon any vehicle unless the occupant of a vehicle is willing to accept it. 
(d)  Cleanup. It shall be the responsibility of any person distributing handbills to maintain the area which they are utilizing free of any litter caused by or related to said handbill distribution. 
(Code 1996, § 131.11; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.12. - Posting notices prohibited. 
No person shall post or affix any notice, poster, or other paper or device, calculated to attract the attention of the public upon any public place, except as may be authorized or required by law. No person except the owner or tenant shall post any such notice on private property, without the permission of the owner or tenant. 
(Code 1996, § 131.12; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Sec. 131.13. - Clearing of litter on private property by city. 
The procedure for the removal of litter from private premises and the charging of expense thereof as a lien upon such property to be collected shall be in accordance with the state statutes. The city manager shall be responsible for the implementation of this enforcement program. 
(Code 1996, § 131.13; Ord. No. 0077, 5-22-1986)  
Title XV - LAND USAGE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Charter reference— Municipal planning, zoning and annexation of property, § VIII. 
State Law reference— Regulation of land use, structures, businesses and related activities, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 211 et seq.; planning and development, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 371 et seq. 
 
CHAPTER 150. - BUILDING REGULATIONS[2] 
Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
State Law reference— Municipal regulation of housing and other structures, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 214. 
 
SUBCHAPTER I. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
Sec. 150.01. - Chief building official. 
(a)  The city manager or his designated representative shall serve as chief building official. Reference to the chief building official in any of the adopted codes shall be deemed to be the city manager or his designated representative. 
(b)  The chief building official is hereby authorized and directed to enforce all the provisions of this chapter. For such purposes, he shall have the powers of a law enforcement officer. The chief building official may appoint such technical officers and inspectors and other employees as he deems necessary from time to time. 
(c)  The chief building official, designated representative or appointed authority, shall have the authority to issue building code violation citations to any person, firm, or corporation violating the provisions and not in proper compliance of this chapter and exercise his enforcement powers as may be deemed necessary for the regulation of such. Citations issued for any such violations, accompanied with the filing of a criminal complaint against the violators will be filed in the municipal court. 
(Code 1996, § 150.02; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 0083, 9-10-1987)  
Sec. 150.02. - Violations. 
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, or corporation to erect, construct, enlarge, alter, repair, move, improve, remove, convert or demolish, equip, use, occupy, or maintain any building or structure or cause or permit the same to be done in violation of this chapter. 
(Code 1996, § 150.03; Ord. No. 0083, 9-10-1987)  
SUBCHAPTER II. - TECHNICAL CODES ADOPTED BY REFERENCE 
 
Sec. 150.15. - International Building Code. 
The International Building Code, 2015 edition, excluding any appendices, as published by the International Code Council, be and is hereby adopted as the building code of the city, for regulating and governing the conditions and maintenance of all property, buildings and structures; by providing the standards for supplied utilities and facilities and other physical things and conditions essential to ensure that structures are safe, sanitary and fit for occupation and use; and the condemnation of buildings and structures unfit for human occupancy and use and the demolition of such structures as herein provided; providing for the issuance of permits and collection of fees therefor; and each and all of the regulations, provisions, penalties, conditions and terms of said building code on file in the office of the city are hereby referred to, adopted, and made a part hereof, as if fully set out in this section. 
(Code 1996, § 150.15; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 107, 2-28-1991; Ord. No. 229, 7-10-2003; Ord. No. 2017-028, § 1, 12-14-2017)  
Sec. 150.16. - One- and two-family dwelling code. 
Detached one- and two-family dwellings and multiple single-family dwellings (townhouses) not more than three stories above grade plane in height with a separate means of egress and their accessory structures shall not be governed by the International Building Code, but instead shall be governed by the One- and Two-Family Dwelling Code, 2015 edition. 
(Code 1996, § 150.16; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 107, 2-28-1991; Ord. No. 229, 7-10-2003; Ord. No. 2017-028, § 1, 12-14-2017)  
Sec. 150.17. - Plumbing code. 
There is hereby adopted by reference the plumbing code passed by the city council on November 29, 1984, as fully as if set out at length herein. 
(Code 1996, § 150.17; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 229, 7-10-2003)  
Sec. 150.18. - International Mechanical Code. 
There is hereby adopted that certain code known as the current edition of the International Mechanical Code and the whole thereof, except as hereinafter amended.  
Sec. 150.19. - Copy of codes in official file. 
A copy of each adopted code shall be placed in an official file in the city secretary's office. 
(Code 1996, § 150.18; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984)  
Sec. 150.20. - Standard specifications for construction. 
(a)  The city council hereby adopts by reference the City of San Antonio Standards and Specifications for Construction (June 2008) with respect to sections 100 through 695 (Excepting Project Scheduling and Management) as an applicable guidance document for construction and subdivision project review. 
(b)  It is further provided that the adoption of this section as guidance shall further authorize the city public works or utilities director to recommend and the city manager to approve (with information copies to the city council) such exceptions as may be deemed necessary and expedient which shall be reasonably adopted to make application and implementation practical and effective for the benefit of the city and its residents. 
(c)  It is further provided that the standard specifications here adopted are a technical resource and criteria for engineering professionals for use in design and construction within and for the city. As design professionals, the designer assumes responsibility for the selection, reference and appropriate application of a proposed project development and implementation. The standard specifications referenced may be augmented by supplemental specifications or modified details produced by a contracted design professional as required by the city. Use of the information hereby adopted is for purpose of setting a standard that shall be reviewed by design professionals and is not intended as a substitute for professional judgment and an appropriate review of design documents with the city's public works or utilities director and consulting professionals. 
(d)  Specifications and drawings for city-sponsored projects may be modified in accordance with these principles. 
(Code 1996, § 150.19; Ord. No. 276, 9-23-2010)  
Sec. 150.21. - Specifications for water and sanitary sewer construction. 
(a)  The city council hereby adopts by reference the San Antonio Water System Specifications for Water and Sanitary Sewer Construction (March 2008) as revised June 2009 (with respect to applicable sized installations and excluding references to water reuse requirements or specifications) as an applicable guidance document for construction and subdivision project review. 
(b)  It is further provided that the adoption by this section as guidance shall further authorize the city public works or utilities director to recommend and the city manager to approve (with information copies to the city council) such exceptions as may be deemed necessary and expedient shall be reasonably adopted to make application and implementation practical and effective for the benefit of the city and its residents. 
(c)  It is further provided that the specifications here adopted are a technical resource and criteria for engineering professionals for use in design and construction within and for the city. As design professionals, the designer assumes responsibility for the selection, reference and appropriate application of proposed project development and implementation. The specifications referenced may be augmented by supplemental specifications or modified details produced by a contracted design professional as required by the city. Use of the information hereby adopted is for purpose of setting a standard that shall be reviewed by design professionals and is not intended as a substitute for professional judgment and an appropriate review of design documents with the city's public works or utilities director and consulting professionals. 
(d)  Specifications and drawings for city-sponsored projects may be modified in accordance with these principles. 
(Code 1996, § 150.20; Ord. No. 275, 9-23-2010)  
SUBCHAPTER III. - ELECTRICAL REGULATIONS 
 
Sec. 150.30. - National electric code adopted by reference; amendments. 
(a)  There is hereby adopted that certain code known as the current edition of the National Electrical Code of the National Fire Protection Association Number 701981 as approved by the American Standards Association, the whole thereof, except as hereinafter amended. 
(b)  Amendments to National Electrical Code. 
(1)  Article 3362, paragraph one, is revised to read as follows: 
Nonmetallic sheathed cable shall be an approved Type NM or NMC in sizes number 12 through two copper conductors. Aluminum or copper clad aluminum conductors shall not be allowed. In addition to the insulated conductors, the cable shall have an approved size of insulated or bare conductors for equipment grounding purposes only. 
(2)  Article 21023 is revised to read as follows: 
21023. Permissible loads. In no case shall the load exceed the branch circuit ampere rating. It shall be acceptable for an individual branch circuit to supply any load for which it is rated. A branch circuit supplying two or more outlets shall supply only the loads specified according to its size in (a) through (c) below and summarized in section 21024 and table 21024, but shall never exceed more than eight outlets or end devices per circuit. 
(Code 1996, § 150.30; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 107, 2-28-1991)  
Sec. 150.31. - Electrical code for one- and two-family dwellings adopted by reference. 
(a)  There is hereby adopted that certain code known as the current edition of the Electrical Code for One- and Two-Family Dwellings, the whole thereof, except as hereinafter amended. 
(b)  Permit fees shall be as specified in section 150.46. 
(Code 1996, § 150.31; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 107, 2-28-1991)  
Sec. 150.32. - Wiring; specifications for materials. 
(a)  Electrical cables, lines, wires, and other methods of transmission of electricity installed by Floresville Electric Light and Power, or any other electrical utility that currently or in the future provides electrical service within the jurisdiction of the city ("utility"), may use aluminum or copper materials so long as the usage of such material is limited to utility owned wire on the electric distribution supply side of the customer's service entrance in order to provide electrical service to both residential and commercial establishments. 
(b)  All other wiring done within the city and its extraterritorial jurisdiction, including, but not limited to, all wiring in residences, commercial buildings, and any and all wiring installed on the customer side of an electric meter, shall be done with copper materials only. 
(Code 1996, § 150.32; Ord. No. 107, 2-28-1991; Ord. No. 2014-21, 12-11-2014)  
SUBCHAPTER IV. - PERMITS 
 
Sec. 150.45. - Permit required; exception for local churches. 
(a)  A permit shall be required prior to commencement of any construction, alterations, installations to include HUD-code manufactured homes, mobile homes, buildings, plumbing, electrical or gas. 
(b)  All local churches established in a permanent structure within the corporate limits or extra-territorial jurisdiction of the city are exempt from the electrical, plumbing, and mechanical (A/C) permit fees but in all cases, are required to pay the flat commercial fee as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time prior to commencement. This provision does not forego the need for the building inspector to conduct all required inspections as are normally required under the adopted building code and compliances met as required in the rules and regulation for the erection, construction, enlargement, alteration and repair of buildings, structures, and mobile homes. 
(c)  A permit shall be required prior to the delivery and use of any temporary construction roll-off waste bin or other temporary waste disposal system intended for use in removing construction and/or demolition debris and which is larger than a standard residential solid waste bin. Permits issued that utilize the temporary waste disposal systems of the city's contracted service provider providing municipal solid waste disposal to the city shall be exempted from any fee for such permit established pursuant to section 150.46. 
(Code 1996, § 150.45; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 83-B, 9-10-1987; Ord. No. 2014-22, 12-11-2014)  
Sec. 150.46. - Permit fee schedule. 
(a)  Where the review of proposed plans and inspection to ensure compliance with the city's zoning requirements and building codes is conducted by a contracted third party, the permit fee charged to build a new building, to add on to an existing building, to remodel, or to alter an existing building, whether residential or commercial, shall be based on the declared valuation of the proposed work. Permit fees based upon such valuation shall be set forth as contained in the table as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time. 
(b)  The city may require the applicant to verify the declared valuation. 
(c)  An additional permit fee shall be required for plumbing, electrical, and mechanical work in the amount as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time per each trade applicable. 
(d)  When submittal documents are required, a plan review fee shall be paid at the time of submitting the submittal documents for plan review. The plan review fees specified in this section are in addition to the building permit fee. Plan review fee shall be 65 percent of the building permit fee as established in subsection (a) of this section. 
(e)  Where the review of proposed plans and inspection to ensure compliance with the city's zoning requirements and building codes is conducted by the city itself, the permit fees charged shall be as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time. 
(f)  Special inspection fees shall be set at the rates as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time. 
(g)  For use of outside consultants, when required, the applicant shall be responsible for the actual costs or the total hourly cost to the city, whichever is the greatest. This cost shall include supervision, overhead, equipment, hourly wages and fringe benefits of the employees involved. 
(Code 1996, § 150.46; Ord. No. 0013, 11-29-1984; Ord. No. 0081, 11-13-1986; Ord. No. 108, 2-28-1991; Ord. No. 128, 9-8-1994; Ord. No. 247, 8-23-2007; Ord. No. 2014-006, 5-8-2014; Ord. No. 2014-22, 12-11-2014; Ord. No. 2015-19, 8-13-2015)  
Sec. 150.47. - Stop-work orders. 
(a)  Upon the issuance of a statement by the city's code enforcement office or city manager of any violation of a federal law, state law, county regulation, city regulation, city ordinance, building code, zoning requirement or municipal franchise agreement, waste and demolition removal, relating to the new construction, alteration, demolition or installation of any construction project, a stop-work order shall be placed upon the subject property. Such stop-work order shall list the violation giving rise to the stop-work order, the date and time of issuance, and the contact information for the city's code enforcement office. 
(b)  A written copy of the stop-work order shall be prominently placed on the main entrance to the subject property, or in any other prominent location, in such a manner as to provide notice to the owner of the property, along with any contractors, subcontractors, agents, or employees thereof, that while the stop-work order is in place, it shall be illegal for any further new construction, alteration, demolition or installation to proceed on the property. 
(c)  The stop-work order shall remain in effect until it is either: 
(1)  Lifted by the city's code enforcement office or city manager; 
(2)  The violation is remedied to the satisfaction of the code enforcement office or city manager; or 
(3)  The matter is appealed to the city council and, following a hearing, the city council lifts the stop-work order. 
(d)  A stop-work order may be appealed to the city council. Upon written notice of appeal delivered to the city's code enforcement office or to the city manager, the recipient of such appeal shall submit such to the city secretary for inclusion on the next regularly scheduled city council meeting (as the Texas Open Meetings Act will allow), or at a regularly scheduled city council meeting of the appellant's choice. Thereupon, a hearing shall be held on the matter, and the city council shall review all information provided by appellant and the details of the alleged violation, and thereupon make a determination as to whether the stop-work order shall be lifted or remain in force until remedied. 
(e)  A violation of a stop-work order is a Class C misdemeanor. 
(f)  Each day of a violation of a stop-work order shall be considered a separate violation, and subject to the penalty set forth in subsection (e) of this section. 
(g)  Compliance with the stop-work order shall be a defense to any prosecution pursuant to subsections (e) and (f) of this section. 
(Code 1996, § 150.47; Ord. No. 2014-10, 12-11-2014)  
Sec. 150.48. - Registration of contractors. 
(a)  Definitions. Words and phrases used in this subchapter shall have the meanings set forth in this section. Words and phrases that are not defined in this subchapter but are defined in other ordinances of the city shall be given the meanings set forth in those ordinances. Other words and phrases shall be given their common, ordinary meaning unless the context clearly requires otherwise. Headings and captions are for reference purposes only, and shall not be used in the interpretation of this subchapter. 
Building inspector means the person appointed by the city council to inspect building activities to ensure compliance with applicable codes, permits and ordinances. The city's building inspector can be a volunteer, employee, agent of another political subdivision, company, corporation, or independent contractor retained by the city. The term "building inspector" includes the code enforcement officer. 
Building official means the person appointed by the city council to receive and review registration applications and ensure compliance with this subchapter. The city's building official can be a volunteer, employee, police officer, agent of another political subdivision, company, corporation, or independent contractor retained by the city. The term includes the code enforcement officer. The city manager shall act as the city's default building official in the absence of a board-appointed person or firm. 
City means the City of Floresville, an incorporated municipality located in Wilson County, Texas, its agents and employees. 
Person means any human individual or corporation, organization, government or governmental subdivision or agency, business trust, estate, trust, partnership, association, and any other legal entity. 
(b)  Registration required. 
(1)  It shall be unlawful for any person to perform or contract to perform for compensation a construction operation within the city limits without first having registered with the city in compliance with this subchapter. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful for any person to perform for compensation a construction operation within the city limits without displaying proof of registration with the city upon request. The only acceptable proof of registration shall be a completed application that is approved and signed by the building official. 
(3)  Exception. Work done by a property owner in a building owned and occupied by the property owner as the property owner's homestead is exempt from this subchapter. 
(c)  Contractors required to register. This subchapter shall apply to persons providing construction services for projects for which a permit is required under city ordinances. Specifically, the following contractors must register with the city: general contractors, plumbing contractors, electrical contractors, and mechanical contractors. 
(d)  Registration. 
(1)  Registration does not substitute for any permit required by law. Nor does registration substitute for any license required by law. 
(2)  In order to register in compliance with this subchapter, contractors must complete the standard contractor registration application designated by the building official. At a minimum, the application form shall contain the following: 
a.  Applicant's name. 
b.  Applicant's place of business address, email address and telephone number. 
c.  Name of owner. 
d.  Type of construction licenses held by applicant. 
e.  License numbers from state department of licensing and regulation, or other applicable state or federal agencies. 
f.  Certificate of Insurance currently in effect demonstrating a minimum general liability coverage level as currently established or as hereafter adopted by resolution of the city council from time to time. 
g.  Copy of sales tax certificate. 
(3)  Registration shall not be approved by the building official until the fee prescribed by the city council has been paid. 
(4)  Persons registered in accordance with this subchapter shall maintain for public inspection a certificate of registration provided by the city. 
(5)  Each permit issued pursuant to this subchapter is subject to annual renewal and payment of renewal fees, as indicated on the attached fee schedule, on January 1 of each year. 
(e)  Enforcement. 
(1)  The city shall have the power to administer and enforce the provisions of this subchapter and the codes adopted by this subchapter as may be required by governing law. Any person violating any provision of this subchapter or the codes herein adopted is subject to suit for injunctive relief as well as prosecution for criminal violations. Any violation of this subchapter is hereby declared to be a nuisance. 
(2)  Any person violating any provision of this subchapter or the codes herein adopted shall be guilty of a Class "C" misdemeanor. 
(3)  Nothing in this subchapter shall be construed as a waiver of the city's right to bring a civil action to enforce the provisions of this subchapter and the codes herein adopted, and to seek remedies as allowed by law, including, but not limited to, the following: 
a.  Injunctive relief to prevent specific conduct that violates this subchapter or to require specific conduct that is necessary for compliance with this subchapter; 
b.  A civil penalty up to $100.00 a day when it is shown that the defendant was actually notified of the provisions of this subchapter and after receiving notice committed acts in violation of this subchapter or failed to take action necessary for compliance with this subchapter. 
(f)  Conflict of provisions. If any provision of this subchapter shall be interpreted as conflicting with or being contrary to a provision in any of the codes adopted by this subchapter, the more stringent requirement shall govern. If it in case of a conflict it is not easily discernible which provision is more stringent, the requirements stated in the text of this subchapter shall govern. 
(Code 1996, § 150.47; Ord. No. 2015-023, § 5, 8-27-2015)  
SUBCHAPTER V. - SUBSTANDARD BUILDINGS[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference— Municipal authority concerning substandard buildings, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code § 214.001 et seq.; additional authority to secure substandard building, V.T.C.A., Local Government Code §§ 214.0011, 214.0015. 
 
Sec. 150.54. - Adoption of V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 214, subch. A. 
The city hereby adopts V.T.C.A., Local Government Code ch. 214, subch. A, and the following minimum standards for the continued use and occupancy of all buildings regardless of the date of their construction; the following provisions for giving proper notice to the owner of a building; and the following provisions for a public hearing to determine compliance of real property, buildings, structures, premises and vacant lots. In the event that any provision of this subchapter conflicts with said chapter 214, subchapter A, or in the event that any provision of said chapter 214, subchapter A has been omitted from this subchapter, the city shall be entitled to pursue its remedies in conformity with said state law, as hereafter amended.  
Sec. 150.55. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this subchapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Substandard buildings means any unoccupied residences or buildings, or occupied buildings or structures which has any or all of the following conditions or defects existing to the extent that the life, health, property, or safety of the public, including unoccupied residences or occupants of buildings or structures are endangered: 
(1)  Whenever any doorway or means of exit is not sufficient to provide safe and adequate means of exit in case of fire. 
(2)  Whenever any walking surface is so unsafe as to not provide adequate means of exit. 
(3)  Whenever the stress in any materials due to all live and dead loads is more than one times the working stress allowed in the adopted International Building Code for new buildings of similar structural purpose or location. 
(4)  Whenever any portion thereof has been damaged by fire, wind, flood, or dilapidation, decay or deterioration to such an extent that the structural strength or stability is materially less than before such occurrence. 
(5)  Whenever any portion thereof is likely to become detached, collapse, fall, or become dislodged and thereby injure persons or damage property. 
(6)  Whenever any portion thereof has wracked, warped, buckled, or settled to such an extent that walls or other portions have materially less resistance to winds than is required in similar new construction. 
(7)  Whenever for any reason the unoccupied residences or buildings, or occupied buildings or structures or portions thereof is manifestly unsafe for the purpose for which it is being used. 
(8)  Whenever the exterior walls or other vertical structural members list, lean, or buckle to such an extent that a plumb line passing through the center of gravity does not fall inside the middle one-third of the base. 
(9)  Whenever the unoccupied residences or buildings, or occupied buildings or structures exclusive of foundation shows 33 percent or more damage of its supporting members or 50 percent of its nonsupporting members, enclosing or outside walls, or coverings. 
(10)  Whenever an unoccupied residence or building, or occupied building or structure used or intending to be used for inhabitation because of inadequate light, air, or sanitary facilities is determined by the city operations director to be unfit for human habitation or in such a condition that is likely to cause sickness or disease. 
(11)  Whenever any unoccupied residences or buildings, or occupied buildings or structures, because of any reason is determined by the fire marshal to be a fire hazard. 
(Code 1996, § 150.55; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975; Ord. No. 137, 9-12-1996)  
Sec. 150.56. - Standards for ordering repair, vacation, or demolition. 
The following standards shall be followed in substance by the authorized official and the city council in ordering repair, vacation, or demolition: 
(1)  If the substandard building can reasonably be repaired so that it will no longer exist in violation of the terms of this subchapter, it shall be ordered repaired. 
(2)  If the substandard building is in such condition as to make it dangerous to the health, safety, or general welfare of the public around an unoccupied residence or occupants of an occupied building or structure it shall be ordered to be vacated. 
(3)  In any case where a substandard building is 50 percent damaged or decayed, or deteriorated from its original value or structure, it shall be demolished and in all cases where an unoccupied residence or occupied building or structure cannot be repaired so that it will no longer exist in violation of the terms of this section, it shall be demolished. In all cases where a substandard building is a fire hazard existing or erected in violation of the terms of this section or any ordinance of the city or statute of the state, it shall be demolished or repaired to the extent that the fire hazard will be eliminated. 
(Code 1996, § 150.56; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
Sec. 150.57. - Enforcement by city manager; inspections; right-of-entry. 
(a)  General administration. The city manager or his designee (building official, fire marshal or authorized official) is hereby authorized to enforce the provisions of this subchapter. 
(b)  Inspections. The city manager or his designee is authorized to make such inspections as may be deemed necessary to enforce the provisions of this subchapter. A written notice of inspection will be mailed to the owners advising of the inspections and may accompany the authorized official during his inspection, if the owner so chooses, to be conducted not less than seven calendar days from the date of such notice. 
(c)  Right of entry. Whenever necessary to make inspections the authorized official must make reasonable effort to gain permission from the unoccupied residence owner or occupants of an occupied building or structure which must include notification once by certified, return receipt requested mail or by publication once in the local newspaper. If entry is refused, the authorized official shall have recourse to every remedy under law to secure entry. 
(Code 1996, § 150.57; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
Sec. 150.58. - Declaration of nuisance; abatement required. 
All unoccupied residences, or occupied buildings and structures or portions thereof which are determined after inspection by the city manager or his designee to be dangerous as defined in this subchapter are hereby declared to be public nuisances and shall be abated by repair, rehabilitation, demolition, or removed in accordance with the procedure specified in sections 150.59 and 150.62. A building which was not a nuisance, and was in fact in compliance with the then building code at the time of its construction may now be a nuisance by reason of its use, deterioration, unsafe or unsanitary conditions, the permitting of its harboring of birds or rodents, occupation by drunkards or other undesirable characters, or becoming obnoxious by reason of odors or looks. 
(Code 1996, § 150.58; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
Sec. 150.59. - Investigation; notice to owner; hearing. 
(a)  Investigation. 
(1)  Whenever it shall come to the attention of the city manager, or any officer of the city, or by reason of complaint of any citizen of the city or city council, that a nuisance or substandard building exists, as herein defined, the authorized official shall upon receipt of such complaint, make a thorough inspection of such alleged nuisance. 
(2)  After such due inspection has been made by the authorized official, he shall make a report for permanent records explaining the circumstances, and his conclusions and/or recommendations. 
(b)  Notice to owner. If, in the opinion of the authorized official, that a building is in fact a nuisance or a substandard building as set out in section 150.55 then the authorized official shall notify the owner in writing in the following manner: 
(1)  Such notice may be served by personal delivery to the owner if he can be located within the city limits, but if he cannot be so located or served after reasonable effort, notice may be served by certified letter addressed to such owner at his last known address, but if such address cannot be ascertained after reasonable effort, notice may be served by publication two times within ten consecutive days in a newspaper of general circulation published in the city. In the case of community property, service upon either the husband or the wife shall be deemed sufficient notice hereunder. 
(2)  If the owner is a corporation, service may be made by delivery of same to any office or place of business of such corporation or any officer of the corporation if such office, place of business, or officer can be located within the city limits, but if such office, place of business, or officer cannot be so located after reasonable effort, service may be made by certified letter addressed to the corporate headquarters address, but if such address cannot be ascertained after reasonable effort, the notice may be served upon the registered agent of the corporation or by publication two times within ten consecutive days in a newspaper of general circulation published in the city. 
(3)  In all cases, if the ownership of the building is unknown, then the notice shall be considered served in addition with other prescribed methods by attaching a copy of it in a place of prominence on such unoccupied residence or occupied building or structure. 
(c)  Hearing. Whether delivered personally, by mail, or by publication, the notice provided for above shall be addressed to the owner, but if the owner is not known, service may be had by publication addressed To the owner of (general description of the property involved.) The notice shall give a general description of the property, state the condition which constitutes a public nuisance, and shall command the owner, or his authorized agent, to appear before the city council and show cause why his unoccupied residence or occupied building or structure should not be declared a nuisance or substandard building and show cause why he should not be ordered to vacate, repair, or destroy such unoccupied residence or occupied building or structure. The date of the hearing shall not be less than ten calendar days after the notice shall have been served. The hearing shall be held at the regular meeting place of the city council during a regular meeting. 
(Code 1996, § 150.59; Ord. No. 97, 9-14-1989)  
Sec. 150.60. - Abatement judgment; order. 
(a)  On the day set in the notice for hearing, the hearing shall be had and on the basis of the hearing, the city council shall make its decision to the effect that the unoccupied residence or occupied building or structure is in fact a nuisance or substandard building or not. The judgment shall further contain an order, as the facts may justify, requiring the owner to either repair such unoccupied residence or occupied building and structure in compliance with the adopted International Building Code (see section 150.15) of the city, or to remove or tear down such unoccupied residences or occupied buildings and structures that such repairs or removal shall be completed within a reasonable time not exceeding 45 calendar days. 
(b)  An extension of 15 calendar days from the 45-day period may be granted, if it is determined by the city manager that a reasonable attempt has been made by the owner or circumstances beyond the owner's control have prevented him from remedying the nuisance or substandard building. Such judgment shall also contain an order to cause a notice of dangerous condition of the building to be affixed in one or more conspicuous places on the exterior of the unoccupied residences, or occupied buildings and structures, and no person shall remove or deface such notice under penalty of law, as herein set out or as set out in other ordinances of the city, as the same exists as the date of such notice. 
(Code 1996, § 150.60; Ord. No. 97, 9-14-1989)  
Sec. 150.61. - Abatement by city; assessment; lien. 
(a)  Assessment. If the owner has failed to comply with the order to repair or remove such unoccupied residence, or occupied building and structure, then the city may cause the unoccupied residence or occupied building and structure to be repaired or removed without delay, and the expenses of such procedure shall be charged against the owner and shall thereupon become a valid and enforceable personal obligation of the owner. A statement of the costs incurred by the city to abate such condition shall be mailed to the owner of such premises, if the owner and mailing address is known, and, if address is not known or owner cannot be found, may be published once in a newspaper of general circulation in the city. The statement shall demand payment within 30 calendar days from the date of receipt (or publication). 
(b)  Nonpayment of statement. In the event that such statement has not been paid within such period, the city manager or his designee may cause a statement to be filed with the county clerk of the expenses incurred to abate and correct such condition of the premises, such statement to be filed in the deed records, and such statement shall be and the city shall have a lien upon the unoccupied residences, or occupied buildings, structure, lot, parcel, or tract of land upon which such expenses were incurred, together with ten percent interest per annum on the delinquent amount from the date such payment was due. For any such expenditures and interest, as aforesaid, suit may be instituted and foreclosure had in the name of the city; and the statement so made, as aforesaid, or certified copy thereof, shall be prima facie proof of the amount expended in any such work; as provided for in Texas Health and Safety Code, sections 342.001 through 342.008. 
(Code 1996, § 150.61; Ord. No. 97, 9-14-1989)  
Sec. 150.62. - Violation; failure to abate; filing of complaint. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for the owner of property determined to contain a dangerous unoccupied residence or occupied building or structure not to abate or arrange to abate such dangerous condition as set forth in section 150.55. 
(b)  If owner does not abate cited dangerous condition or to make arrangement to do so, the city manager or his designee shall file a complaint with municipal court and the prosecutor of the municipal court assigned such duties shall prosecute the case. Such complaint may be filed each 60 days until abatement or arrangement is accomplished. 
(Code 1996, § 150.62; Ord. No. 97, 9-14-1989)  
Sec. 150.63. - Refusal to comply with order; interference with enforcement. 
Any person who shall willfully refuse or fail to leave an unoccupied residence, or occupied building or structure which has been ordered vacated under the terms of this subchapter, or who shall enter an unoccupied residence, or occupied building or structure which has been ordered vacated under the terms of this subchapter, or who shall enter an area around such unoccupied residence, or occupied building or structure that has been declared to be dangerous and notice of which declaration shall have been posted, and any person who shall interfere with or hinder the vacation, repair, or demolition of any unoccupied residence, or occupied building or structure under the terms of this subchapter shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. In case the owner or occupant of any substandard building ordered vacated, repaired, or demolished under the terms of this subchapter shall be a corporation, the president, vice-president, secretary, or treasurer of such corporation, or any manager, agent, or employee of such corporation, shall be also severally liable for the penalties herein provided. 
(Code 1996, § 150.63; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
Sec. 150.64. - Resort to courts. 
Nothing in this section shall be construed as abridging the right of the city to resort to the courts of this state for the enforcement of this subchapter, or of the rights of any owner to resort to the courts of this state in an attempt to enjoin the enforcement of this subchapter. 
(Code 1996, § 150.64; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
Sec. 150.65. - Duty of city attorney. 
It shall be the duty of the city attorney to enforce the orders of the city council or the authorized official, upon appeal, by filing action in the appropriate court of the state when so authorized by the city council. 
(Code 1996, § 150.65; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
Sec. 150.66. - Remedies cumulative. 
The enumeration of remedies for the suppression of a public nuisance as provided in this subchapter are not to be deemed as exclusive, but as cumulative. 
(Code 1996, § 150.66; Ord. No. 97, 9-25-1975)  
CHAPTER 151. - FLOOD DAMAGE PREVENTION[4] 
Footnotes: 
--- (4) --- 
State Law reference— Soil and water conservation, V.T.C.A., Agriculture Code ch. 201; emergency management, V.T.C.A., Government Code ch. 418; Flood Control and Insurance Act, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 16.311 et seq.; local rules, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 16.318; local governments must adopt ordinances necessary for jurisdiction to qualify for National Flood Insurance Program, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 16.3145; political subdivision to comply with Federal requirements, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 16.315. 
 
SUBCHAPTER I. - GENERAL PROVISIONS 
 
Sec. 151.01. - Statutory authorization. 
The legislature of the state has in the Flood Control Insurance Act, V.T.C.A., Water Code § 16.315, delegated the responsibility of local governmental units to adopt regulations designed to minimize flood losses. Therefore, the city council does ordain this chapter. 
(Code 1996, § 151.01; Ord. No. 0087, 12-17-1987; Ord. No. 196, 5-9-2002; Ord. No. 278, 9-23-2010)  
Sec. 151.02. - Findings of fact. 
(a)  The flood hazard areas of the city are subject to periodic inundation which results in loss of life and property, health and safety hazards, disruption of commerce and governmental services, and extraordinary public expenditures for flood protection and relief, all of which adversely affect the public health, safety, and general welfare. 
(b)  These flood losses are created by the cumulative effect of obstructions in floodplains which cause an increase in flood heights and velocities, and by the occupancy of flood hazards areas by uses vulnerable to floods and hazardous to other lands because they are inadequately elevated, floodproofed, or otherwise protected from flood damage. 
(Code 1996, § 151.02; Ord. No. 0087, 12-17-1987; Ord. No. 196, 5-9-2002; Ord. No. 278, 9-23-2010)  
Sec. 151.03. - Statement of purpose. 
It is the purpose of this chapter to promote the public health, safety, and general welfare and to minimize public and private losses due to flood conditions in specific areas by provisions designed to: 
(1)  Protect human life and health. 
(2)  Minimize expenditure of public money for costly flood control projects. 
(3)  Minimize the need for rescue and relief efforts associated with flooding and generally undertaken at the expense of the general public. 
(4)  Minimize prolonged business interruptions. 
(5)  Minimize damage to public facilities and utilities such as water and gas mains, electric, telephone and sewer lines, streets and bridges located in floodplains. 
(6)  Help maintain a stable tax base by providing for the sound use and development of floodprone areas in such a manner as to minimize future flood blight areas. 
(7)  Ensure that potential buyers are notified that property is in a flood area. 
(Code 1996, § 151.03; Ord. No. 0087, 12-17-1987; Ord. No. 196, 5-9-2002; Ord. No. 278, 9-23-2010)  
Sec. 151.04. - Methods of reducing flood losses. 
In order to accomplish its purposes, this chapter uses the following methods: 
(1)  Restrict or prohibit uses that are dangerous to health, safety or property in times of flood, or cause excessive increases in flood heights or velocities. 
(2)  Require that uses vulnerable to floods, including facilities which serve such uses, be protected against flood damage at the time of initial construction. 
(3)  Control the alteration of natural floodplains, stream channels, and natural protective barriers, which are involved in the accommodation of floodwaters. 
(4)  Control filling, grading, dredging, and other development which may increase flood damage. 
(5)  Prevent or regulate the construction of flood barriers which will unnaturally divert floodwaters or which may increase flood hazards to other lands. 
(Code 1996, § 151.04; Ord. No. 0087, 12-17-1987; Ord. No. 196, 5-9-2002; Ord. No. 278, 9-23-2010)  
Sec. 151.05. - Definitions. 
Unless specifically defined below, words or phrases used in this chapter shall be interpreted to give them the meaning they have in common usage and to give this chapter its most reasonable application. 
Alluvial fan flooding means flooding occurring on the surface of an alluvial fan or similar landform which originates at the apex and is characterized by high velocity flows; active processes of erosion, sediment transport, and deposition; and unpredictable flow paths. 
Apex means a point on an alluvial fan or similar landform below which the flow path of the major stream that formed the fan becomes unpredictable and alluvial fan flooding can occur. 
Appurtenant structure means a structure which is on the same parcel of property as the principal structure to be insured and the use of which is incidental to the use of the principal structure. 
Area of future conditions flood hazard means the land area that would be inundated by the one percent annual chance (100-year) flood based on future conditions hydrology. 
Area of shallow flooding means a designated AO, AH, AR/AO, AR/AH, or VO zone on a community's flood insurance rate map (FIRM) with a one percent or greater annual chance of flooding to an average depth of one to three feet where a clearly defined channel does not exist, where the path of flooding is unpredictable and where velocity flow may be evident. Such flooding is characterized by ponding or sheet flow. 
Area of special flood hazard means the land in the floodplain within a community subject to a one percent or greater chance of flooding in any given year. The area may be designated as Zone A on the flood hazard boundary map (FHBM). After detailed rate making has been completed in preparation for publication of the FIRM, Zone A usually is refined into zones A, AO, AH, A130, AE, A99, AR, AR/A130, AR/AE, AR/AO, AR/AH, AR/A, VO, V130, VE or V. 
Base flood means the flood having a one percent chance of being equaled or exceeded in any given year.
